# ⚡ 2. BACKEND + SYSTEM DESIGN AWS QUESTIONS

## ❓ Q6. Design a scalable backend using AWS

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
Scalable backend = System jo **badhte traffic ke saath automatically handle kar sake** without breaking. AWS provides services that scale automatically.

**Intermediate:**  
Scalability = Ability to handle increased load by adding resources. Two types:
- **Vertical scaling** (bigger instance) → Limited, has ceiling
- **Horizontal scaling** (more instances) → Unlimited, true cloud scalability

**Advanced (Internal Working):**

```
Scalability Types Deep Dive:

Vertical Scaling (Scale Up):
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ t2.micro (1 vCPU, 1GB RAM)                                 │
│      │                                                      │
│      ▼ (upgrade)                                           │
│ t2.large (2 vCPU, 8GB RAM)                                 │
│      │                                                      │
│      ▼ (upgrade)                                           │
│ m5.4xlarge (16 vCPU, 64GB RAM)                             │
│                                                             │
│ Limitations:                                               │
│ - Max instance size (AWS limit, e.g., 448 vCPU)            │
│ - Downtime during upgrade                                   │
│ - Cost grows exponentially                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Horizontal Scaling (Scale Out):
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ 1 instance → 10 instances → 100 instances → 1000 instances │
│                                                             │
│ No theoretical limit!                                      │
│ Requirements:                                              │
│ - Stateless applications                                   │
│ - Load balancer                                            │
│ - Shared state (database/cache)                            │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Complete Scalable Architecture (Production Ready)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                         GLOBAL SCALABILITY LAYER                            │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                      Route 53 (DNS + Health Checks)                  │   │
│  │  - Latency-based routing (route to nearest region)                   │   │
│  │  - Weighted routing (A/B testing, blue/green)                        │   │
│  │  - Failover routing (active-passive DR)                              │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                      CloudFront (CDN)                                │   │
│  │  - Static assets cached at 400+ edge locations                       │   │
│  │  - Dynamic content acceleration (optimized routes)                   │   │
│  │  - DDoS protection (AWS Shield)                                      │   │
│  │  - Custom SSL certificates                                           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
└────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┘
                                     │
                    ┌────────────────┴────────────────┐
                    │                                 │
                    ▼                                 ▼
        ┌───────────────────────┐        ┌───────────────────────┐
        │   Region 1 (Primary)  │        │   Region 2 (DR)       │
        │   e.g., us-east-1     │        │   e.g., us-west-2     │
        │                       │        │                       │
        │  ┌─────────────────┐  │        │  ┌─────────────────┐  │
        │  │  WAF (Web ACL)  │  │        │  │  WAF            │  │
        │  └────────┬────────┘  │        │  └────────┬────────┘  │
        │           │           │        │           │           │
        │           ▼           │        │           ▼           │
        │  ┌─────────────────┐  │        │  ┌─────────────────┐  │
        │  │  API Gateway    │  │        │  │  API Gateway    │  │
        │  │  - Rate limit   │  │        │  │  - Rate limit   │  │
        │  │  - Auth (JWT)   │  │        │  │  - Auth (JWT)   │  │
        │  │  - Throttling   │  │        │  │  - Throttling   │  │
        │  │  - Request      │  │        │  │  - Request      │  │
        │  │    transform    │  │        │  │    transform    │  │
        │  └────────┬────────┘  │        │  └────────┬────────┘  │
        │           │           │        │           │           │
        │           ▼           │        │           ▼           │
        │  ┌─────────────────┐  │        │  ┌─────────────────┐  │
        │  │  Application    │  │        │  │  Application    │  │
        │  │  Load Balancer  │  │        │  │  Load Balancer  │  │
        │  │  (ALB)          │  │        │  │  (ALB)          │  │
        │  │  - Path-based   │  │        │  │  - Path-based   │  │
        │  │    routing      │  │        │  │    routing      │  │
        │  │  - SSL          │  │        │  │  - SSL          │  │
        │  │    termination  │  │        │  │    termination  │  │
        │  └────────┬────────┘  │        │  └────────┬────────┘  │
        │           │           │        │           │           │
        │           ▼           │        │           ▼           │
        │  ┌─────────────────┐  │        │  ┌─────────────────┐  │
        │  │  Auto Scaling   │  │        │  │  Auto Scaling   │  │
        │  │  Group (EC2)    │  │        │  │  Group (EC2)    │  │
        │  │                 │  │        │  │                 │  │
        │  │  ┌─────┐ ┌─────┐│  │        │  │  ┌─────┐ ┌─────┐│  │
        │  │  │EC2-1│ │EC2-2││  │        │  │  │EC2-1│ │EC2-2││  │
        │  │  └──┬──┘ └──┬──┘│  │        │  │  └──┬──┘ └──┬──┘│  │
        │  │     │       │   │  │        │  │     │       │   │  │
        │  │  ┌──┴───────┴──┐│  │        │  │  ┌──┴───────┴──┐│  │
        │  │  │  EFS (shared││  │        │  │  │  EFS (shared││  │
        │  │  │  storage)   ││  │        │  │  │  storage)   ││  │
        │  │  └─────────────┘│  │        │  │  └─────────────┘│  │
        │  └────────┬────────┘  │        │  └────────┬────────┘  │
        │           │           │        │           │           │
        └───────────┼───────────┘        └───────────┼───────────┘
                    │                                 │
        ┌───────────┼───────────┐        ┌───────────┼───────────┐
        │           │           │        │           │           │
        ▼           ▼           ▼        ▼           ▼           ▼
    ┌───────┐  ┌───────┐  ┌───────┐  ┌───────┐  ┌───────┐  ┌───────┐
    │ RDS   │  │Elasti-│  │S3     │  │ RDS   │  │Elasti-│  │S3     │
    │Primary│  │Cache  │  │(Cross-│  │Standby│  │Cache  │  │(Cross-│
    │Multi- │  │(Redis)│  │region │  │(Read  │  │(Redis)│  │region │
    │AZ     │  │Cluster│  │replica│  │replica│  │Cluster│  │replica│
    └───────┘  └───────┘  └───────┘  └───────┘  └───────┘  └───────┘

    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    │                    ASYNC PROCESSING LAYER                    │
    ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
    │                                                             │
    │  ┌─────────┐    ┌─────────┐    ┌─────────┐    ┌─────────┐  │
    │  │   SQS   │───→│   SQS   │───→│ Lambda  │───→│   SNS   │  │
    │  │ (Queue) │    │ (DLQ)   │    │ Worker  │    │ (Notify)│  │
    │  └─────────┘    └─────────┘    └─────────┘    └─────────┘  │
    │                                                             │
    │  Dead Letter Queue: Failed messages after 3 retries         │
    │  Lambda retries: 2 times with exponential backoff           │
    └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Step-by-Step Request Flow

```
User Request Flow through Scalable System:

Step 1: DNS Resolution
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
User types: api.myapp.com
Route 53: Returns CloudFront edge location IP (closest to user)

Step 2: CDN/Caching Layer
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CloudFront checks cache:
├── If static asset (CSS/JS/image) → Return from edge (5-10ms)
├── If dynamic API request → Forward to origin (API Gateway)

Step 3: Security & Rate Limiting
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
WAF (Web Application Firewall):
├── Check for SQL injection, XSS, bad bots
├── IP reputation check
├── Rate limiting: 1000 requests per IP per minute

Step 4: API Gateway (Entry Point)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
API Gateway:
├── Authenticate JWT token (Cognito/custom Lambda authorizer)
├── Validate request schema
├── Apply throttling (burst: 2000, rate: 1000 per second)
├── Route to appropriate backend:
│   ├── /api/v1/orders → Order service (EC2)
│   ├── /api/v1/users → User service (Lambda)
│   └── /api/v1/products → Product service (EC2 + cache)
└── Log request to CloudWatch

Step 5: Load Balancing
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
ALB (Application Load Balancer):
├── Terminates SSL (TLS 1.3)
├── Checks target group health:
│   ├── Health check endpoint: /health (every 30 sec)
│   ├── Healthy threshold: 2 successes
│   └── Unhealthy threshold: 3 failures
├── Routing algorithm: Round-robin with least outstanding requests
├── Sticky sessions disabled (stateless design)
└── Forward to EC2 instance in same AZ (minimize latency)

Step 6: Application Processing
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
EC2 Instance (Spring Boot / Node.js):
├── Process business logic
├── Check Redis cache first (session, product data)
│   ├── Cache hit → Return (2-5ms)
│   └── Cache miss → Query RDS (10-50ms)
├── Write to database (RDS Primary)
├── Publish event to SQS (async tasks)
└── Return response (200 OK)

Step 7: Async Processing (Decoupled)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SQS Queue:
├── Message stored (retention: 14 days)
├── Lambda poller picks up (batch size: 10)
├── Process: Send email, update search index, generate reports
├── On failure → Retry 3 times with backoff (1s, 2s, 4s)
└── Still failing → Move to DLQ (Dead Letter Queue) for manual review

Step 8: Response Path
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Response travels back:
EC2 → ALB → API Gateway → CloudFront → User
Total latency: 50-200ms (p99)
```

### 4. Scaling Strategies (Production Patterns)

**Pattern 1: Auto Scaling Policies**

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              Auto Scaling Group Configuration               │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                             │
│ Launch Template:                                           │
│   AMI: custom-spring-boot-ami-2024-01-15                   │
│   Instance Type: t3.large (2 vCPU, 8GB RAM)                │
│   User Data: #!/bin/bash                                   │
│              systemctl start myapp                         │
│                                                             │
│ Scaling Policies (Multiple):                               │
│                                                             │
│ 1. Target Tracking (Primary):                              │
│    Metric: CPUUtilization                                  │
│    Target: 70%                                             │
│    Scale out: Add 1 instance when CPU > 70% for 2 min     │
│    Scale in: Remove 1 when CPU < 30% for 10 min           │
│                                                             │
│ 2. Simple Scaling (For SQS):                               │
│    Metric: SQS queue depth                                 │
│    Threshold: > 1000 messages                              │
│    Action: Add 2 instances                                 │
│    Cooldown: 300 seconds                                   │
│                                                             │
│ 3. Scheduled Scaling (For predictable peaks):              │
│    Mon-Fri 9 AM: Scale to 20 instances                     │
│    Mon-Fri 6 PM: Scale to 5 instances                      │
│    Weekend: Scale to 2 instances                           │
│                                                             │
│ Instance Warm-up: 60 seconds (before health checks)        │
│ Termination Policy: Oldest instance first                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Pattern 2: Database Scaling**

```
Read Scaling (RDS Read Replicas):
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                             │
│  Write traffic (10%) ──→ RDS Primary (Multi-AZ)            │
│                              │                              │
│                    (Async replication)                      │
│                              │                              │
│         ┌────────────────────┼────────────────────┐        │
│         │                    │                    │        │
│         ▼                    ▼                    ▼        │
│   Read Replica 1        Read Replica 2        Read Replica 3│
│   (AZ1)                (AZ2)                (AZ3)          │
│         │                    │                    │        │
│         └────────────────────┼────────────────────┘        │
│                              │                              │
│                    Read traffic (90%)                       │
│                    Distributed across replicas              │
│                                                             │
│ Application logic:                                         │
│ - Write queries: Use primary endpoint                       │
│ - Read queries: Use reader endpoint (load balancer)        │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Sharding (Horizontal Partitioning):
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                             │
│  User ID hash % 4:                                         │
│                                                             │
│  User ID 1-25M    User ID 25M-50M   User ID 50M-75M  etc.  │
│      │                 │                 │                  │
│      ▼                 ▼                 ▼                  │
│  Shard 1           Shard 2           Shard 3                │
│  (RDS)             (RDS)             (RDS)                  │
│                                                             │
│ Application: Routing shard based on user_id % num_shards   │
│ Challenge: Rebalancing (consistent hashing)                │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Pattern 3: Caching Strategy**

```
Multi-Layer Caching:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                             │
│  Level 1: Client Cache (Browser)                           │
│  - Cache-Control: max-age=3600                             │
│  - ETags for validation                                     │
│                                                             │
│  Level 2: CDN Cache (CloudFront)                           │
│  - Static assets: 1 year                                   │
│  - API responses: 5-60 seconds (for read-heavy endpoints)  │
│  - Invalidation: ~10-15 minutes                            │
│                                                             │
│  Level 3: Application Cache (ElastiCache Redis)            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │ Cache Patterns:                                      │   │
│  │                                                      │   │
│  │ 1. Cache-Aside (Lazy Loading):                      │   │
│  │    Read: Check cache → Miss → Read DB → Store cache │   │
│  │    Write: Write DB → Invalidate cache               │   │
│  │                                                      │   │
│  │ 2. Write-Through:                                   │   │
│  │    Write: Write DB AND cache together               │   │
│  │    Read: From cache always                          │   │
│  │                                                      │   │
│  │ 3. Write-Behind:                                    │   │
│  │    Write: Write to cache only → Async write to DB   │   │
│  │    (High risk of data loss)                         │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                             │
│  Cache Data Examples:                                      │
│  - User sessions: TTL 1 hour                               │
│  - Product catalog: TTL 1 hour (invalidate on update)     │
│  - Rate limiting counters: TTL 1 minute                    │
│  - Distributed locks: TTL 30 seconds                       │
│                                                             │
│  Level 4: Database Cache (RDS buffer pool)                 │
│  - MySQL InnoDB buffer pool                                │
│  - PostgreSQL shared buffers                               │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 5. Failure Handling & Reliability

```
Failure Scenarios & Mitigations:

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Scenario 1: EC2 Instance Failure                           │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Detection: Health check fails (3 consecutive failures)     │
│ Action: Auto Scaling terminates unhealthy instance         │
│ Recovery: Launches new instance (2-3 minutes)              │
│ During recovery: Traffic routed to other instances         │
│ Data loss? None (stateless app, EBS persists but new       │
│            instance gets fresh EBS)                        │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Scenario 2: Entire AZ Outage                               │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Detection: ALB health checks (30 seconds)                  │
│ Action: ALB stops routing to instances in failed AZ        │
│ Recovery: Remaining AZs handle all traffic                 │
│ Auto Scaling: Launches instances in healthy AZs            │
│ RDS: Automatic failover to standby in other AZ (60 sec)    │
│ Data loss? None (RDS sync replication)                     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Scenario 3: RDS Primary Failure                            │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Detection: RDS health checks (30 seconds)                  │
│ Action: Automatic failover to standby replica              │
│ Recovery Time: 30-120 seconds                              │
│ During failover: Write operations fail (retry on client)   │
│ Reads: Still work if using reader endpoint                 │
│ Data loss? None (sync replication)                         │
│ After failover: Old primary becomes new standby            │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Scenario 4: Regional Outage (DR)                           │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Detection: Route 53 health checks (60 seconds)             │
│ Action: Failover to secondary region                       │
│ Recovery: Manual or automated (Route 53 failover record)   │
│ RTO: 5-15 minutes (if automated)                          │
│ RPO: Seconds to minutes (async cross-region replication)   │
│ Cost: Double infrastructure (hot standby) or lower (cold)  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 6. Security Considerations

```
Security Layers in Scalable Backend:

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Layer 1: Network Security                                  │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ - VPC with public/private subnets                          │
│ - Security Groups (EC2, RDS, ALB)                          │
│ - NACLs (subnet-level)                                     │
│ - VPC endpoints for S3/DynamoDB                            │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Layer 2: Identity & Access                                 │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ - IAM roles for EC2 (no hardcoded keys)                    │
│ - Cognito for user authentication                          │
│ - API Gateway Lambda authorizer (JWT validation)           │
│ - Fine-grained permissions (least privilege)               │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Layer 3: Data Security                                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ - Encryption in transit: TLS 1.3 (ALB, API Gateway)        │
│ - Encryption at rest: RDS (AWS KMS), S3 (SSE-S3)           │
│ - Secrets Manager for DB passwords, API keys               │
│ - Parameter Store for configuration                        │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Layer 4: Application Security                              │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ - WAF (SQL injection, XSS protection)                      │
│ - Rate limiting (API Gateway)                              │
│ - Input validation (application level)                     │
│ - Output encoding (prevent XSS)                            │
│ - SQL injection prevention (parameterized queries)         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 7. Cost Optimization Strategies

```
Cost Optimization for Scalable Backend:

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Compute Optimization                                       │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ - Use Spot instances for non-critical workloads (70% off)  │
│ - Reserved instances for baseline capacity (40-60% off)    │
│ - Auto Scaling to match demand (no over-provisioning)      │
│ - Right-sizing (CloudWatch + Trusted Advisor)              │
│ - Graviton processors (20% cheaper, better perf)           │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Storage Optimization                                       │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ - S3 Intelligent-Tiering for unknown access patterns       │
│ - Lifecycle policies (move to Glacier after 30 days)       │
│ - EBS gp3 instead of gp2 (lower cost, better performance)  │
│ - Delete unused snapshots, old logs                        │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Database Optimization                                      │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ - Read replicas for read-heavy workloads                   │
│ - DynamoDB auto scaling (not over-provisioning)            │
│ - RDS reserved instances (for production)                  │
│ - Graviton for RDS (cost savings)                          │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Data Transfer Optimization                                 │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ - Keep traffic within same AZ when possible                │
│ - Use CloudFront for static assets (reduces origin load)   │
│ - VPC endpoints (no NAT gateway cost for S3/DynamoDB)      │
│ - Avoid cross-AZ data transfer (costs add up)              │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 8. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"For a scalable backend, I'd use a multi-layer architecture. At the edge, CloudFront with Route 53 for global routing. Then API Gateway for rate limiting and auth. Behind that, ALB with Auto Scaling Groups of EC2 instances. For data, RDS Multi-AZ with read replicas, ElastiCache Redis for caching, and S3 for static assets. Async tasks go through SQS to Lambda workers. This design handles 10K+ requests per second, scales horizontally, and has 99.99% availability."*

**Key points to mention:**

1. **Stateless design** - Sessions in Redis, not on EC2
2. **Horizontal scaling** - Add instances, not bigger ones
3. **Caching at every layer** - CDN, Redis, DB cache
4. **Async decoupling** - SQS for background tasks
5. **Multi-AZ** - No single point of failure
6. **Auto scaling** - Based on real metrics (CPU, queue depth)
7. **Read replicas** - Scale reads separately from writes

### 9. Follow-up Questions

| Question | Answer |
|----------|--------|
| *"How do you handle database schema changes without downtime?"* | Use online schema migration tools (gh-ost, pt-online-schema-change). Blue-green database deployment. |
| *"What happens when cache and DB are inconsistent?"* | Use write-through or cache invalidation. Acceptable inconsistency window vs strong consistency (choose based on use case). |
| *"How do you implement distributed tracing?"* | AWS X-Ray, OpenTelemetry, or Jaeger. Trace ID propagates through all services. |
| *"How do you test scalability?"* | Load testing (JMeter, Locust), chaos engineering (AWS Fault Injection Simulator), canary deployments. |

### 10. Short Summary

```
Scalable Backend Architecture - Quick Reference:

Edge Layer:
- Route 53 (DNS + routing)
- CloudFront (CDN + DDoS)

Entry Layer:
- WAF (security)
- API Gateway (rate limit, auth)
- ALB (load balancing)

Compute Layer:
- Auto Scaling Group (EC2)
- Launch templates
- Multiple AZs

Data Layer:
- RDS Multi-AZ + Read Replicas
- ElastiCache Redis (caching)
- S3 (static/files)

Async Layer:
- SQS (buffering)
- Lambda (workers)
- DLQ (failed messages)

Key Principles:
1. Stateless services
2. Cache everything
3. Decouple with queues
4. Auto scale based on metrics
5. Multi-AZ for HA
6. Monitor everything (CloudWatch)

Interview Hook:
"Scalability isn't just about handling more traffic. 
It's about handling failure gracefully, maintaining low latency 
under load, and optimizing cost. I design for 10x growth."
```

---

## ❓ Q7. How do you handle high traffic in AWS?

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
High traffic = Bahut saare users ek saath request bhej rahe hain. Handle karne ke liye:
- Auto scaling (automatic instances add karo)
- Caching (repeat requests ko cache se serve karo)
- CDN (content ko users ke paas rakho)

**Intermediate:**  
High traffic handling requires **vertical** (more resources) and **horizontal** (more instances) scaling, plus **architectural patterns** like caching, queueing, and sharding.

**Advanced (Traffic Patterns):**

```
Types of High Traffic:

1. Gradual Growth (Predictable):
   ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   │ Traffic                                               │
   │    ↑                                                  │
   │    │      ┌────────────────────────┐                  │
   │    │     ╱                          ╲                 │
   │    │    ╱                            ╲                │
   │    │   ╱                              ╲               │
   │    │  ╱                                ╲              │
   │    │ ╱                                  ╲             │
   │    │────────────────────────────────────────→ Time   │
   │ Solution: Auto Scaling (gradual scale out)           │
   └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

2. Flash Sale / Viral Event (Spiky):
   ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   │ Traffic                                               │
   │    ↑                                                  │
   │    │     ┌────┐                                       │
   │    │     │    │                                       │
   │    │    ╱│    │╲                                      │
   │    │   ╱ │    │ ╲                                     │
   │    │  ╱  │    │  ╲                                    │
   │    │ ╱   │    │   ╲                                   │
   │    │────────────────────────────────────────→ Time   │
   │ Solution: Pre-warmed auto scaling, aggressive caching │
   └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

3. DDoS Attack (Malicious):
   ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   │ Traffic (attack)                                      │
   │    ↑                                                  │
   │    │ ┌────────────────────────────────────────┐       │
   │    │ │                                        │       │
   │    │ │         (Attack traffic)               │       │
   │    │ │                                        │       │
   │    │ └────────────────────────────────────────┘       │
   │    │          (Normal traffic)                         │
   │    │────────────────────────────────────────→ Time   │
   │ Solution: AWS Shield, WAF, rate limiting              │
   └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. High Traffic Handling Strategies (Complete)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                        HIGH TRAFFIC HANDLING STRATEGIES                      │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 1: CACHING (Most Important)                                      │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Without Cache:                    With Cache:                         │ │
│  │  User → EC2 → DB (50ms)           User → CloudFront (5ms)              │ │
│  │       ↑                              │                                 │ │
│  │       └── Each request hits DB       └── Cache hit (90% requests)      │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Result: 1000 req/sec → DB dies     Result: 10,000 req/sec handled    │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Cache Layers:                                                        │ │
│  │  - Browser Cache (Cache-Control headers)                              │ │
│  │  - CDN Cache (CloudFront - 400+ edge locations)                       │ │
│  │  - Application Cache (Redis - 5-10ms)                                 │ │
│  │  - Database Cache (RDS buffer pool - 1-5ms)                           │ │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 2: AUTO SCALING                                                   │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Traffic Spike:                                                        │ │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │ │
│  │  │ 100 req/sec → 10 instances → 1000 req/sec → 100 instances      │   │ │
│  │  │                                                               │   │ │
│  │  │ Scale-out triggers:                                           │   │ │
│  │  │ - CPU > 70% for 2 minutes                                     │   │ │
│  │  │ - Memory > 80% for 2 minutes                                  │   │ │
│  │  │ - SQS queue depth > 1000                                      │   │ │
│  │  │ - Custom metric (requests per second)                         │   │ │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Pre-warming:                                                         │ │
│  │  - Scale up BEFORE traffic hits (scheduled scaling)                   │ │
│  │  - Maintain buffer of 20% extra capacity                              │ │
│  │  - Use predictive scaling (ML-based)                                  │ │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 3: LOAD BALANCING                                                 │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Distribution Algorithms:                                             │ │
│  │  - Round Robin: Simple, even distribution                            │ │
│  │  - Least Connections: Send to instance with fewest active connections │ │
│  │  - Least Response Time: Send to fastest responding instance           │ │
│  │  - IP Hash: Stickiness (for sessions without external cache)         │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  ALB Features:                                                        │ │
│  │  - Path-based routing (/api/* → service A, /static/* → service B)    │ │
│  │  - Host-based routing (api.myapp.com vs admin.myapp.com)             │ │
│  │  - Weighted routing (95% v1, 5% v2 for canary)                       │ │
│  │  - Slow start (gradually increase traffic to new instances)          │ │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 4: QUEUE-BASED BUFFERING                                          │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Problem: Traffic spike > processing capacity                         │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Solution: SQS Queue                                                  │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Incoming Traffic:      Queue:        Workers:                        │ │
│  │  ┌─────┐                ┌─────┐       ┌─────┐                        │ │
│  │  │10K  │───────────────→│████│──────→│100  │                        │ │
│  │  │req/s│                │████│       │req/s│                        │ │
│  │  └─────┘                │████│       └─────┘                        │ │
│  │                         └─────┘                                      │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Benefits:                                                            │ │
│  │  - Protects backend from overload                                     │ │
│  │  - Smooths out traffic spikes                                         │ │
│  │  - Allows async processing                                            │ │
│  │  - Messages persisted (no data loss)                                  │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Queue Monitoring:                                                    │ │
│  │  - ApproximateNumberOfMessages (if > 10K → scale workers)             │ │
│  │  - ApproximateAgeOfOldestMessage (if > 5 min → alert)                 │ │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 5: DATABASE OPTIMIZATION                                          │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Read-Heavy Workload:                                                 │ │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │ │
│  │  │ Primary (writes) → Replica 1 (reads) → Replica 2 (reads)       │ │ │
│  │  │                   → Replica 3 (reads) → Replica 4 (reads)       │ │ │
│  │  │                                                                 │ │ │
│  │  │ 10% writes, 90% reads → 1 primary + 4 replicas = 5x read perf  │ │ │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Write-Heavy Workload:                                                │ │
│  │  - Sharding (horizontal partitioning)                                 │ │
│  │  - Use DynamoDB (auto-sharding)                                       │ │
│  │  - Queue writes (batch them)                                          │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Connection Pooling:                                                  │ │
│  │  - HikariCP (default 10 connections) → Increase to 50-100            │ │
│  │  - RDS max_connections: (memory / 125) * 2 for PostgreSQL            │ │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 6: CDN & EDGE COMPUTING                                           │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  Without CDN:                   With CDN:                             │ │
│  │  User in India ─────────────────→│                                     │ │
│  │  (300ms latency)                 │  User → Edge (5ms)                 │ │
│  │       │                           │    │                               │ │
│  │       ▼                           │    ▼ (cache miss only)            │ │
│  │  Server in US (Origin)            │  Origin (US) - 150ms              │ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  100% traffic to origin           10% traffic to origin (90% cache hit)│ │
│  │                                                                        │ │
│  │  CloudFront Features:                                                 │ │
│  │  - Lambda@Edge (run code at edge)                                     │ │
│  │  - Dynamic content acceleration (optimized AWS backbone)              │ │
│  │  - Field-level encryption (sensitive data)                            │ │
│  │  - Geo-restriction (serve only to specific countries)                 │ │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Complete High Traffic Architecture

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                      HIGH TRAFFIC ARCHITECTURE (10K+ req/sec)               │

│  │  │  └─────┘ └─────┘ └─────┘ └─────┘ └─────┘ └─────┘           │   │   │

│  │  │  ┌─────────┐  ┌─────────┐  ┌─────────┐  ┌─────────┐        │   │   │
│  │  │  │Shard 1  │  │Shard 2  │  │Shard 3  │  │Shard 4  │        │   │   │

│  │  │ +Read    │  │ Scaling  │  │          │  │ Query    │           │   │
│  │  │ Replicas │  │          │  │          │  │          │           │   │
│  │  └──────────┘  └──────────┘  └──────────┘  └──────────┘           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │

│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐           │   │
│  │  │ SQS      │→│ Lambda   │→│ SNS      │  │ Event    │           │   │
│  │  │ (Queue)  │  │ (Worker) │  │ (Notify) │  │ Bridge   │           │   │
│  │  └──────────┘  └──────────┘  └──────────┘  └──────────┘           │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Dead Letter Queue: Failed messages storage                           │   │
│  │  Retry Policy: 3 attempts with exponential backoff (1s, 2s, 4s)      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4. Real-World Performance Numbers

```
Performance Targets for High Traffic System:

Metric                    | Target (p99)    | How to Achieve
─────────────────────────┼─────────────────┼────────────────────────────
API Response Time        | < 100ms         | Caching + CDN + Optimized DB
Database Query Latency   | < 10ms          | Indexes + Read Replicas
Cache Hit Ratio          | > 90%           | Proper TTL + Cache Aside
Auto Scaling Latency     | < 2 minutes     | Pre-warming + Predictive
Failover Time (RDS)      | < 60 seconds    | Multi-AZ + Monitoring
SQS Processing Delay     | < 5 seconds     | Enough workers + Batching
CDN Cache Hit Ratio      | > 95%           | Long TTL + Invalidation

Real Example (Production):
- Peak traffic: 50,000 req/sec
- EC2 instances: 200 t3.large (Auto Scaling)
- RDS: 1 primary + 5 read replicas (db.r5.4xlarge)
- Redis: 8 shards (cache.m5.2xlarge each)
- CloudFront: 95% cache hit ratio
- Avg latency: 45ms (p99: 120ms)
- Cost: ~$15,000/month
```

### 5. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"For high traffic, I use a defense-in-depth approach. First, CloudFront CDN offloads 90%+ of static traffic. Then API Gateway with rate limiting protects against spikes. Behind that, ALB with Auto Scaling Groups - we pre-warm before known peaks. ElastiCache Redis reduces database load by 80%+. For write-heavy operations, we buffer through SQS to smooth out spikes. RDS read replicas handle query load. We monitor everything with CloudWatch and have auto-scaling based on CPU, memory, and queue depth. In one project, this handled 10x traffic spike during a flash sale with zero downtime."*

**Key points to emphasize:**

1. **Cache first** - Most important for read-heavy workloads
2. **Scale horizontally** - Not vertically
3. **Queue for spikes** - SQS as shock absorber
4. **Read replicas** - Separate read/write paths
5. **Monitor everything** - CloudWatch alarms for proactive scaling
6. **Test with load** - JMeter/Locust before production

### 6. Short Summary

```
High Traffic Handling - Cheat Sheet:

Strategy            | When to Use                    | AWS Service
────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────┼─────────────
Caching             | Read-heavy, repeatable queries | CloudFront, Redis
Auto Scaling        | Traffic varies unpredictably   | ASG, EC2
Load Balancing      | Multiple instances             | ALB/NLB
Queueing            | Traffic spikes, async tasks    | SQS
Read Replicas       | Read-heavy workload            | RDS
CDN                 | Global users, static assets    | CloudFront
Sharding            | Write-heavy, huge dataset      | DynamoDB

Key Metrics to Monitor:
- CPU Utilization (target: 60-70%)
- Memory Usage (target: <80%)
- SQS Queue Depth (alert if >10K)
- Database Connections (avoid exhaustion)
- Cache Hit Ratio (target: >90%)

Interview Hook:
"Handling high traffic is about preventing failure before it happens. 
Cache aggressively, scale proactively, and always have a fallback. 
The cloud lets you scale, but you need the right architecture first."
```
