# 🚀 3. DATABASE & STORAGE (Very Important)

## ❓ Q10. RDS vs DynamoDB

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
- **RDS** = Relational database (like MySQL, PostgreSQL). Data tables mein rows aur columns mein rehta hai. Joins, complex queries possible.
- **DynamoDB** = NoSQL database. Key-value aur document storage. Fast, scalable, but complex queries limited.

**Intermediate:**  
RDS = **SQL database** with fixed schema, ACID transactions, joins, and complex queries.  
DynamoDB = **NoSQL database** with flexible schema, key-value access, automatic sharding, and predictable latency.

**Advanced (Internal Working):**

```
RDS Internal Architecture (PostgreSQL/MySQL):
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                             │
│  RDS Instance (db.r5.large):                               │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Operating System (Amazon Linux)                    │   │
│  │  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │   │
│  │  │  Database Engine (PostgreSQL 15)              │ │   │
│  │  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  Shared Buffers (25% of RAM)            │  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  - Caches table pages, indexes          │  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  - LRU (Least Recently Used) eviction   │  │ │   │
│  │  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │   │
│  │  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  Write-Ahead Log (WAL)                  │  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  - All writes go here first             │  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  - Flushed to disk every 200ms          │  │ │   │
│  │  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │   │
│  │  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  Query Planner                         │  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  - Parses SQL                          │  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  - Optimizes query (chooses index)     │  │ │   │
│  │  │  │  - Executes and returns results        │  │ │   │
│  │  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │   │
│  │  └───────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │   │
│  │                                                      │   │
│  │  EBS Volume (gp3/io2):                             │   │
│  │  - Up to 64,000 IOPS (io2)                        │   │
│  │  - 16,000 IOPS (gp3)                              │   │
│  │  - Data persisted even if instance fails          │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                             │
│  Limitations:                                              │
│  - Single instance has max CPU/RAM/IOPS                    │
│  - To scale: Read replicas (async) or bigger instance      │
│  - Max storage: 64TB (io2)                                │
│  - Max connections: (~5000 for db.r5.large)               │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

DynamoDB Internal Architecture:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                             │
│  DynamoDB Table: users                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Partition Key: user_id (hash)                      │   │
│  │  Sort Key: timestamp (range) - optional             │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                             │
│  Internal: Consistent Hashing                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                      │   │
│  │  user_id hash % num_partitions = partition number   │   │
│  │                                                      │   │
│  │  Example:                                           │   │
│  │  user_id "123" → hash(123) = 456789                │   │
│  │  456789 % 4 = 1 → Partition 1                      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                             │
│  Data Distribution:                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                      │   │
│  │  Partition 1    Partition 2    Partition 3    Partition 4│
│  │  ┌─────┐        ┌─────┐        ┌─────┐        ┌─────┐   │
│  │  │SSD  │        │SSD  │        │SSD  │        │SSD  │   │
│  │  │     │        │     │        │     │        │     │   │
│  │  │Data │        │Data │        │Data │        │Data │   │
│  │  │Repl │        │Repl │        │Repl │        │Repl │   │
│  │  └─────┘        └─────┘        └─────┘        └─────┘   │
│  │     │              │              │              │      │
│  │     └──────────────┴──────────────┴──────────────┘      │
│  │                    │                                    │
│  │            Replicated across 3 AZs                      │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                             │
│  Auto-scaling:                                              │
│  - Partitions split when too large (>10GB)                 │
│  - New partitions added when throughput increases          │
│  - Rebalancing happens automatically                       │
│  - No downtime during scaling                              │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Complete Comparison Table

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    RDS vs DYNAMODB - Complete Comparison                    │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Feature              | RDS (PostgreSQL/MySQL)    | DynamoDB               │
│  ─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼────────────────────────│
│  **Data Model**       | Relational (tables,       | Key-value + Document   │
│                       | rows, columns, joins)     | (JSON)                 │
│  **Schema**           | Fixed (define columns     | Flexible (schemaless)  │
│                       | before inserting)          |                        │
│  **Scaling**          | Vertical (bigger instance) | Horizontal (auto      │
│                       | + Read replicas            | sharding)              │
│  **Max Throughput**   | Limited by instance       | Unlimited (theoretically)│
│                       | (~100K writes/sec)         | (>10M writes/sec)      │
│  **Query Capability** | Complex SQL (JOINs,        | Simple (GetItem,       │
│                       | GROUP BY, subqueries)      | Query, Scan)           │
│  **Indexes**          | Multiple indexes on       | Primary key (hash +    │
│                       | any column                 | range) + GSI/LSI       │
│  **Transactions**     | ACID (full support)       | ACID (limited to 25    │
│                       |                           | items, 4MB)            │
│  **Latency (p99)**    | 10-50ms (can be lower     | Single-digit ms        │
│                       | with caching)              | (consistent)           │
│  **Pricing**          | Per hour + storage + IOPS | Per RCU/WCU + storage  │
│  **Managed**          | Yes (AWS manages OS,      | Yes (fully serverless) │
│                       | patching, backups)         |                        │
│  **Max Item Size**    | Row size limited by       | 400KB per item         │
│                       | DB engine (1.6GB in PG)    |                        │
│  **Backup**           | Automated (35 days) +     | Point-in-time recovery │
│                       | Snapshots                  | (35 days)              │
│  **Global Tables**    | Cross-region read replicas | Active-Active cross-   │
│                       | (manual)                   | region (automatic)     │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Performance Deep Dive

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    PERFORMANCE CHARACTERISTICS                              │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  RDS Query Performance:                                                    │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Query Type                    | With Index    | Without Index       │   │
│  │  ──────────────────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────────────│   │
│  │  SELECT * FROM users WHERE id=1| 1-5ms        | 10-50ms             │   │
│  │  SELECT * FROM orders WHERE    | 5-20ms        | 100ms-2s            │   │
│  │    user_id=1 ORDER BY date     |               | (full scan)         │   │
│  │  JOIN users, orders, products  | 20-100ms      | >2s (cartesian)     │   │
│  │  COUNT(*) GROUP BY category    | 100-500ms     | >5s                 │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Index Types:                                                         │   │
│  │  - B-Tree (default)                                                  │   │
│  │  - Hash (equality only)                                              │   │
│  │  - GIN (full text search)                                            │   │
│  │  - GiST (geospatial)                                                 │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  DynamoDB Access Patterns:                                                 │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Operation                     | Latency (p99)  | Cost (RCU/WCU)     │   │
│  │  ──────────────────────────────┼────────────────┼───────────────────│   │
│  │  GetItem (by primary key)      | 2-5ms          | 1 RCU (4KB)        │   │
│  │  Query (by partition key)      | 5-10ms         | RCU per item       │   │
│  │  Query with filter             | 10-20ms        | RCU for all scanned│   │
│  │  Scan (full table)             | >100ms         | High (entire table)│   │
│  │  PutItem (insert/update)       | 5-10ms         | 1 WCU (1KB)        │   │
│  │  BatchGetItem (100 items)      | 20-50ms        | 100 RCU            │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Best Practices:                                                      │   │
│  │  - Use GetItem for point lookups                                     │   │
│  │  - Use Query with partition key for 1:N relationships                │   │
│  │  - Avoid Scan at all costs (use GSI instead)                         │   │
│  │  - Denormalize data to avoid "joins"                                 │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4. Real-World Decision Framework

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              RDS vs DYNAMODB - When to Choose Which?                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  CHOOSE RDS WHEN:                                                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ✅ You need complex queries (JOINs, GROUP BY, subqueries)           │   │
│  │  ✅ Your data is highly relational (normalized)                      │   │
│  │  ✅ You need ACID transactions across multiple tables                │   │
│  │  ✅ You have reporting/analytics requirements                        │   │
│  │  ✅ Schema is stable and well-defined                                │   │
│  │  ✅ You need foreign key constraints                                 │   │
│  │  ✅ Existing team knows SQL well                                     │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Real Examples:                                                       │   │
│  │  - E-commerce: Orders, Products, Customers (relational)              │   │
│  │  - Banking: Accounts, Transactions, Ledgers (ACID critical)          │   │
│  │  - CRM: Contacts, Deals, Activities (complex queries)                │   │
│  │  - Reporting: Monthly sales reports (aggregations)                   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  CHOOSE DYNAMODB WHEN:                                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ✅ You need massive scale (>100K writes/sec)                        │   │
│  │  ✅ Access pattern is known (mostly key-value lookups)               │   │
│  │  ✅ You need single-digit millisecond latency                        │   │
│  │  ✅ Schema is flexible or evolving                                   │   │
│  │  ✅ Traffic is spiky (auto-scaling)                                  │   │
│  │  ✅ You want serverless (no instance management)                     │   │
│  │  ✅ Data is denormalized (can duplicate)                             │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Real Examples:                                                       │   │
│  │  - Shopping cart (high throughput, key by user_id)                   │   │
│  │  - Session store (fast lookups, TTL)                                 │   │
│  │  - Leaderboard (DynamoDB with Redis for ranking)                     │   │
│  │  - IoT device data (millions of writes/sec)                          │   │
│  │  - User profile (simple key-value)                                   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  HYBRID APPROACH (Best of both worlds):                                    │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Use DynamoDB for high-throughput operations:                        │   │
│  │  - Shopping cart (100K updates/sec)                                  │   │
│  │  - Session store (50K reads/sec)                                     │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Use RDS for complex queries and reporting:                          │   │
│  │  - Order history with JOINs                                          │   │
│  │  - Monthly analytics                                                 │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Data synchronization:                                               │   │
│  │  - DynamoDB Streams → Lambda → RDS (ETL)                             │   │
│  │  - Or use both (DynamoDB for live, RDS for analytics)                │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 5. Pricing Comparison (Real Numbers)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    PRICING COMPARISON (us-east-1)                           │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  RDS (PostgreSQL, db.r5.large, 2 vCPU, 16GB RAM):                         │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  On-Demand: $0.288/hour = $207/month                               │   │
│  │  Reserved (1 year, no upfront): $0.173/hour = $125/month           │   │
│  │  Reserved (3 years, all upfront): $0.115/hour = $83/month          │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Storage: gp3, 100GB = $10/month                                   │   │
│  │  Backup storage: 100GB = $10/month                                 │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Total: $100-250/month (depending on reserved)                      │   │
│  │  Per request cost: ~$0.000001 per query (very cheap)                │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Good for: Steady traffic, 1M-100M queries/month                    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  DynamoDB (Standard):                                                      │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  On-Demand (pay per request):                                       │   │
│  │  - Write requests: $1.25 per million WCU                           │   │
│  │  - Read requests: $0.25 per million RCU                            │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Provisioned (reserved capacity):                                   │   │
│  │  - Write capacity: $0.00065 per WCU/hour ($0.468 per month)        │   │
│  │  - Read capacity: $0.00013 per RCU/hour ($0.094 per month)         │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Storage: $0.25 per GB/month                                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Example costs:                                                     │   │
│  │  - 10M reads/month (on-demand): $2.50                              │   │
│  │  - 1M writes/month (on-demand): $1.25                              │   │
│  │  - 100GB storage: $25/month                                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Good for: Spiky traffic, low to medium volume                      │   │
│  │  Expensive for: High volume (>1B requests/month)                   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Cost Comparison (1M reads + 100K writes + 100GB storage):                 │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  RDS (reserved): $100-150/month                                    │   │
│  │  DynamoDB (on-demand): $2.50 + $0.125 + $25 = $27.625/month        │   │
│  │  DynamoDB (provisioned): $25 + $0.47 + $0.10 = $25.57/month        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Winner for low volume: DynamoDB                                     │   │
│  │  Winner for high volume (>100M requests): RDS                       │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 6. Migration Path (RDS → DynamoDB)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              MIGRATING FROM RDS TO DYNAMODB (When needed)                   │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Step 1: Identify Access Patterns                                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  RDS Table: orders                                                  │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  Queries:                                                   │    │   │
│  │  │  1. SELECT * FROM orders WHERE order_id = ? (90% traffic)   │    │   │
│  │  │  2. SELECT * FROM orders WHERE user_id = ? (9% traffic)     │    │   │
│  │  │  3. Complex analytics queries (1% traffic)                  │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Step 2: Design DynamoDB Table                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Primary Key:                                                       │   │
│  │  - Partition Key: order_id                                          │   │
│  │  - Sort Key: (none)                                                 │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Global Secondary Index (GSI):                                      │   │
│  │  - Partition Key: user_id                                           │   │
│  │  - Sort Key: order_date                                             │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Denormalization:                                                   │   │
│  │  - Include user_name, product_names (duplicate data)                │   │
│  │  - Avoid joins (store what you need)                                │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Step 3: Data Migration                                                    │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  AWS DMS (Database Migration Service):                              │   │
│  │  - Continuous replication                                           │   │
│  │  - Minimal downtime                                                 │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Or ETL with Glue:                                                  │   │
│  │  - Read from RDS                                                    │   │
│  │  - Transform data (denormalize)                                     │   │
│  │  - Write to DynamoDB                                                │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Step 4: Handle Complex Queries                                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Option 1: Keep RDS for analytics (hybrid)                          │   │
│  │  Option 2: Use DynamoDB + OpenSearch (Elasticsearch)                │   │
│  │  Option 3: Use DynamoDB + Athena (query S3 export)                  │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 7. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"I choose RDS when I need complex queries, joins, and ACID transactions. For example, our order management system used PostgreSQL because we needed to join orders, products, customers, and run monthly reports. I choose DynamoDB when I need massive scale and predictable low latency. For our shopping cart, we switched from RDS to DynamoDB and saw latency drop from 50ms to 5ms, and it auto-scales during flash sales. The key is understanding your access patterns - DynamoDB is not a replacement for RDS, it's a different tool for different problems."*

**Common mistakes to avoid:**

1. Using DynamoDB for complex queries (scan is expensive!)
2. Using RDS for massive scale (vertical scaling has limits)
3. Not understanding DynamoDB's 400KB item limit
4. Forgetting that RDS needs maintenance windows
5. Not designing access patterns before choosing DynamoDB

### 8. Follow-up Questions

| Question | Answer |
|----------|--------|
| *"Can DynamoDB do joins?"* | No, you denormalize data. Store related data together in the same item. |
| *"What's a DynamoDB GSI?"* | Global Secondary Index - alternate partition key for different access pattern. |
| *"How many read replicas can RDS have?"* | Up to 5 (but can cascade for more). |
| *"What's DynamoDB's consistency model?"* | Eventual consistency (default) or strong consistency (double cost). |
| *"Can RDS auto-scale storage?"* | Yes, up to 64TB. No downtime. |

### 9. Short Summary

```
RDS vs DynamoDB - Quick Reference:

RDS (SQL):
- Fixed schema, complex queries, ACID
- Scale vertically + read replicas
- Good for: Relational data, reporting, transactions
- Pricing: Per hour (cheap for high volume)

DynamoDB (NoSQL):
- Flexible schema, key-value access
- Scale horizontally (auto sharding)
- Good for: High throughput, low latency, simple access
- Pricing: Per request (cheap for low volume)

Decision Tree:
Need joins/transactions? → RDS
Need >100K writes/sec? → DynamoDB
Complex queries? → RDS
Predictable low latency? → DynamoDB
Schema evolving? → DynamoDB
Reporting/analytics? → RDS

Interview Hook:
"RDS and DynamoDB solve different problems. 
I use RDS for the 'source of truth' with complex relationships, 
and DynamoDB for high-scale, low-latency access patterns. 
Often, I use both - DynamoDB for live traffic, RDS for analytics."
```

---

## ❓ Q11. When to use DynamoDB?

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
DynamoDB use karo jab tumhe **fast**, **scalable**, aur **simple key-value access** chahiye. Agar tumhara access pattern known hai (mostly get by ID), to DynamoDB perfect hai.

**Intermediate:**  
DynamoDB excels at **single-digit millisecond latency** at any scale. Best for **known access patterns** where you query by primary key or simple indexes.

**Advanced (Access Patterns First):**

```
DynamoDB Design Principle: "Access patterns first, not data model first"

Traditional RDS Design:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  1. Define normalized schema (users, orders, products)     │
│  2. Define relationships (foreign keys)                    │
│  3. Write queries to join data                            │
│  4. Optimize with indexes                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

DynamoDB Design:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  1. List all access patterns (how will you read data?)    │
│  2. Denormalize data to fit those patterns                │
│  3. Design primary key + GSIs to support patterns         │
│  4. Duplicate data if needed (single table design)        │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Ideal Use Cases (With Examples)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    DYNAMODB IDEAL USE CASES                                 │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  USE CASE 1: Shopping Cart                                                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Access Pattern:                                                    │   │
│  │  - Get cart by user_id (90%)                                        │   │
│  │  - Add/remove items (10%)                                           │   │
│  │  - No complex queries                                               │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  DynamoDB Table: shopping_cart                                      │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  Partition Key: user_id                                     │    │   │
│  │  │  Sort Key: (none)                                           │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  Attributes:                                                │    │   │
│  │  │  - items (list of products)                                 │    │   │
│  │  │  - total_price                                              │    │   │
│  │  │  - last_updated (TTL: 7 days)                               │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Why DynamoDB:                                                      │   │
│  │  - Single user lookup (perfect for GetItem)                         │   │
│  │  - High write throughput (add/remove items)                         │   │
│  │  - TTL automatically deletes abandoned carts                        │   │
│  │  - <5ms latency                                                    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  USE CASE 2: Session Store                                                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Access Pattern:                                                    │   │
│  │  - Get session by session_id (95%)                                  │   │
│  │  - Update session (5%)                                              │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  DynamoDB Table: sessions                                           │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  Partition Key: session_id                                   │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  Attributes:                                                │    │   │
│  │  │  - user_id                                                  │    │   │
│  │  │  - data (JSON)                                              │    │   │
│  │  │  - expires_at (TTL)                                         │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Why DynamoDB:                                                      │   │
│  │  - Fast point lookups (2-3ms)                                      │   │
│  │  - Automatic TTL (session expiration)                              │   │
│  │  - Scales to millions of sessions                                  │   │
│  │  - Cheaper than Redis for large datasets                           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  USE CASE 3: Leaderboard                                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Access Pattern:                                                    │   │
│  │  - Get top 100 players (80%)                                        │   │
│  │  - Get player rank (15%)                                            │   │
│  │  - Update score (5%)                                                │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  DynamoDB Table: leaderboard                                        │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  Partition Key: game_id                                      │    │   │
│  │  │  Sort Key: score (GSI)                                       │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  Attributes:                                                │    │   │
│  │  │  - player_id                                                │    │   │
│  │  │  - player_name                                              │    │   │
│  │  │  - score                                                    │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Why DynamoDB:                                                      │   │
│  │  - GSI on score allows sorted queries                               │   │
│  │  - High write throughput (millions of score updates)                │   │
│  │  - Consistent low latency                                           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  USE CASE 4: IoT Device Data                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Access Pattern:                                                    │   │
│  │  - Get latest reading for device (70%)                              │   │
│  │  - Get history for device (20%)                                     │   │
│  │  - Batch write millions of readings (10%)                           │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  DynamoDB Table: device_readings                                    │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  Partition Key: device_id                                    │    │   │
│  │  │  Sort Key: timestamp                                         │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  Attributes:                                                │    │   │
│  │  │  - temperature                                              │    │   │
│  │  │  - humidity                                                 │    │   │
│  │  │  - battery_level                                            │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Why DynamoDB:                                                      │   │
│  │  - Time-series data (partition by device, sort by time)             │   │
│  │  - Write up to 1,000 WCU per partition (scale with devices)         │   │
│  │  - Query for specific device's history (fast)                       │   │
│  │  - TTL to auto-delete old data                                      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  USE CASE 5: User Profile                                                 │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Access Pattern:                                                    │   │
│  │  - Get profile by user_id (95%)                                     │   │
│  │  - Update profile (5%)                                              │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  DynamoDB Table: user_profiles                                      │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  Partition Key: user_id                                      │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  Attributes (flexible schema):                              │    │   │
│  │  │  - name, email, preferences (JSON), settings (JSON)         │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Why DynamoDB:                                                      │   │
│  │  - Flexible schema (add new fields anytime)                         │   │
│  │  - Fast point lookups                                               │   │
│  │  - Cheaper than RDS for this pattern                               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. When NOT to Use DynamoDB

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    WHEN TO AVOID DYNAMODB                                   │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  ❌ Complex Queries (JOINs, aggregations, full-text search)                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  "Find all users who bought product X in last 30 days and live in   │   │
│  │   New York, then calculate average order value"                     │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Solution: Use RDS or DynamoDB + OpenSearch (Elasticsearch)         │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ❌ Ad-hoc Queries (Reporting, Analytics)                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  "I don't know what questions I'll ask tomorrow"                    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Solution: Use RDS for reporting, or export DynamoDB to S3 + Athena │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ❌ Large Items (>400KB)                                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  "Storing product catalog with images (2MB each)"                   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Solution: Store in S3, reference in DynamoDB                       │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ❌ Strongly Consistent Cross-Item Transactions                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  "Transfer $100 from Account A to Account B"                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Solution: Use RDS (native ACID) or DynamoDB transactions (max 25   │   │
│  │  items, 4MB)                                                        │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ❌ Low Throughput (<100 requests/second)                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  "Internal admin panel with 10 users"                               │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Solution: RDS may be cheaper (DynamoDB minimum cost)               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4. DynamoDB Single Table Design (Advanced)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│           SINGLE TABLE DESIGN (Advanced DynamoDB Pattern)                   │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Instead of multiple tables (users, orders, products), use ONE table:      │
│                                                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Table: app_data                                                    │   │
│  │  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │   │
│  │  │  Partition Key: PK (string)                                    │  │   │
│  │  │  Sort Key: SK (string)                                         │  │   │
│  │  │  Attributes: data (JSON), GSI1PK, GSI1SK, etc.                │  │   │
│  │  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Data Modeling:                                                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Entity Type    | PK              | SK              | GSI1PK         │   │
│  │  ───────────────┼─────────────────┼─────────────────┼────────────────│   │
│  │  User           | USER#123        | PROFILE#123     | -              │   │
│  │  Order          | USER#123        | ORDER#456       | ORDER#456      │   │
│  │  Product        | PRODUCT#789     | METADATA#789    | -              │   │
│  │  UserOrderIndex | USER#123        | ORDER#456       | ORDER#456      │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Access Patterns:                                                     │   │
│  │  1. Get user by ID: Query(PK = "USER#123")                           │   │
│  │  2. Get all orders for user: Query(PK = "USER#123", SK starts_with("ORDER#"))│
│  │  3. Get specific order: Query(PK = "USER#123", SK = "ORDER#456")     │   │
│  │  4. Get order by order ID: Query(GSI1PK = "ORDER#456")               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Benefits:                                                                 │
│  - One table to manage                                                    │
│  - No joins (everything denormalized)                                     │
│  - All access patterns in one place                                       │
│  - Cheaper (fewer GSIs)                                                   │
│                                                                             │
│  Drawbacks:                                                                │
│  - Harder to understand                                                   │
│  - Overkill for simple apps                                               │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 5. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"I use DynamoDB when access patterns are simple and predictable. For example, our user session store - we only need get by session ID and set with TTL. DynamoDB gives us 2-3ms latency and auto-scales to millions of sessions. I avoid DynamoDB for complex queries or reporting. The key insight is that with DynamoDB, you design your access patterns first, then your table. It's not like RDS where you normalize data and then figure out queries."*

**Key points to mention:**

1. **Access patterns first** - Know how you'll read data
2. **Single-digit millisecond latency** - At any scale
3. **Auto-scaling** - Perfect for spiky traffic
4. **Flexible schema** - Add fields without migration
5. **TTL** - Automatic data expiration
6. **DynamoDB Streams** - Real-time change data capture

### 6. Short Summary

```
DynamoDB - Quick Reference:

Use When:
✅ Simple key-value lookups
✅ Known access patterns
✅ High throughput needed
✅ Single-digit ms latency
✅ Flexible schema
✅ Auto-scaling required
✅ TTL needed (session expiry)

Avoid When:
❌ Complex queries (JOINs, aggregations)
❌ Ad-hoc reporting
❌ Large items (>400KB)
❌ Complex transactions
❌ Low throughput (cheaper with RDS)

Key Concepts:
- Partition Key = Hash key (distribution)
- Sort Key = Range key (sorting)
- GSI = Alternate partition key
- LSI = Alternate sort key (same partition)
- RCU/WCU = Read/Write Capacity Units
- DynamoDB Streams = CDC (Change Data Capture)

Interview Hook:
"DynamoDB is for when you know exactly how you'll access your data.
Design your access patterns first, then build your table.
Don't try to use it like a relational database - that's a common mistake."
```

- DB scaling strategies
