## ❓ Q12. What is read replica?

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
Read replica = Database ki **copy** jo sirf **read** (SELECT) queries handle karti hai. Original database (primary) writes handle karta hai. Reads ko distribute karke performance improve hoti hai.

**Intermediate:**  
Read replica = Asynchronous copy of primary database. Used to **offload read traffic**, improve read performance, and provide **high availability** (can be promoted to primary).

**Advanced (Internal Working):**

```
Read Replica Internal Architecture (RDS PostgreSQL):
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  PRIMARY INSTANCE (db.r5.large)          READ REPLICA (db.r5.large)        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────┐        ┌─────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Write Query:               │        │  Read Query:                │   │
│  │  INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE     │        │  SELECT * FROM users        │   │
│  │           │                 │        │           │                  │   │
│  │           ▼                 │        │           ▼                  │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────┐        │        │  ┌─────────────────┐        │   │
│  │  │  Transaction    │        │        │  │  Query Engine   │        │   │
│  │  │  Log (WAL)      │        │        │  └────────┬────────┘        │   │
│  │  └────────┬────────┘        │        │           │                  │   │
│  │           │                 │        │           ▼                  │   │
│  │           │ (WAL streaming) │        │  ┌─────────────────┐        │   │
│  │           └─────────┬───────┘        │  │  Replica Buffer │        │   │
│  │                     │                │  └────────┬────────┘        │   │
│  │                     │ (Async)        │           │                  │   │
│  │                     ▼                │           │                  │   │
│  │              Replication Slot        │           │ (WAL apply)       │   │
│  │                     │                │           ▼                  │   │
│  │                     └────────────────┼───┐  ┌─────────────────┐     │   │
│  │                                      │   │  │  Replication    │     │   │
│  │                                      │   └─→│  Apply Process  │     │   │
│  │                                      │      └─────────────────┘     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────┘        └─────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Key Points:                                                               │
│  - Asynchronous replication (no impact on primary performance)             │
│  - Replica lag: typically <100ms, can spike during heavy writes           │
│  - Read replicas can be in different AZs or regions                       │
│  - Can promote replica to primary (for DR or failover)                    │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Read Replica Architecture Patterns

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    READ REPLICA ARCHITECTURE PATTERNS                       │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN 1: Single Region, Multiple AZs (Most Common)                      │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │                         us-east-1 Region                             │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │                                                              │    │   │
│  │  │  AZ-1                    AZ-2                    AZ-3        │    │   │
│  │  │  ┌─────────────┐        ┌─────────────┐        ┌─────────┐  │    │   │
│  │  │  │  PRIMARY    │        │  Read       │        │  Read   │  │    │   │
│  │  │  │  (RDS)      │───┐    │  Replica 1  │───┐    │  Replica│  │    │   │
│  │  │  │  Writes     │   │    │  (Reads)    │   │    │  2      │  │    │   │
│  │  │  └─────────────┘   │    └─────────────┘   │    │  (Reads) │  │    │   │
│  │  │                    │                      │    └─────────┘  │    │   │
│  │  │                    │ (Async replication)  │                 │    │   │
│  │  │                    └──────────────────────┘                 │    │   │
│  │  │                                                              │    │   │
│  │  │  Application:                                                │    │   │
│  │  │  - Writes → Primary endpoint                                │    │   │
│  │  │  - Reads → Reader endpoint (load balancer across replicas)  │    │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN 2: Cross-Region Read Replicas (Global Read Scaling)               │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  us-east-1 (Primary)           eu-west-1 (Read Replica)             │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────┐           ┌─────────────────┐                  │   │
│  │  │  PRIMARY        │           │  Read Replica   │                  │   │
│  │  │  (RDS)          │──(Async)─→│  (Cross-region) │                  │   │
│  │  └─────────────────┘           └─────────────────┘                  │   │
│  │         │                              │                             │   │
│  │         │ (Writes)                      │ (Reads)                     │   │
│  │         ▼                              ▼                             │   │
│  │  US Users (200ms latency)      EU Users (5ms latency)                │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Use Case: Global applications, disaster recovery                     │   │
│  │  Trade-off: Cross-region replication cost + higher lag (1-2 sec)     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN 3: Cascading Read Replicas (Very High Read Load)                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  PRIMARY ──→ Replica A ──→ Replica B                                │   │
│  │                │              │                                      │   │
│  │                │              │                                      │   │
│  │            Read Load      Read Load                                  │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Why cascade?                                                        │   │
│  │  - Primary can only handle 5 direct replicas                         │   │
│  │  - Cascade for 10+ replicas                                          │   │
│  │  - Warning: Increased lag (each hop adds delay)                      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN 4: Read Replica for Reporting (Isolate Workloads)                 │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  PRIMARY                    Reporting Replica                        │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────┐        ┌─────────────────┐                     │   │
│  │  │  OLTP (Online    │        │  OLAP (Analytics)│                     │   │
│  │  │  Transaction    │───┐    │  - Complex JOINs │                     │   │
│  │  │  Processing)    │   │    │  - Aggregations  │                     │   │
│  │  │                 │   │    │  - Full table    │                     │   │
│  │  │  - Fast inserts │   │    │    scans        │                     │   │
│  │  │  - Point queries│   │    │                  │                     │   │
│  │  └─────────────────┘   │    └─────────────────┘                     │   │
│  │                        │                                             │   │
│  │                        └── (Replication)                             │   │
│  │                                                                       │   │
│  │  Benefit: Heavy analytics queries don't affect production traffic    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Read Replica Lag & Monitoring

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    READ REPLICA LAG - UNDERSTANDING                         │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  What is Replica Lag?                                                      │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Lag = Time difference between primary and replica                   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Example:                                                           │   │
│  │  Time 00:00:00 - Primary: User inserts record                       │   │
│  │  Time 00:00:00 - Replica: Doesn't have it yet                       │   │
│  │  Time 00:00:05 - Replica: Receives and applies update               │   │
│  │  Lag = 5 seconds                                                     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Causes of High Lag:                                                       │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  1. Heavy write workload on primary                                 │   │
│  │     - Too many INSERTs/UPDATEs for replica to keep up               │   │
│  │     - Solution: Scale primary or batch writes                       │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  2. Under-provisioned replica                                       │   │
│  │     - Replica smaller than primary                                  │   │
│  │     - Solution: Same size or larger replica                         │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  3. Long-running queries on replica                                 │   │
│  │     - Replica busy with complex SELECTs                             │   │
│  │     - Solution: Separate reporting replica                          │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  4. Network latency (cross-region)                                  │   │
│  │     - Cross-region adds 50-200ms lag                                │   │
│  │     - Solution: Acceptable for DR, not for live reads               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Monitoring (CloudWatch Metrics):                                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Metric: ReplicaLag (seconds)                                       │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Alarm:                                                             │   │
│  │  - Warning: Lag > 60 seconds for 5 minutes                          │   │
│  │  - Critical: Lag > 300 seconds for 2 minutes                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Action:                                                            │   │
│  │  - Investigate write workload                                       │   │
│  │  - Increase replica size                                            │   │
│  │  - Promote replica if lag never catches up                          │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4. Read Replica vs Multi-AZ (Important Distinction)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              READ REPLICA vs MULTI-AZ - COMPLETE COMPARISON                 │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Feature                    | Read Replica          | Multi-AZ              │
│  ───────────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼──────────────────────│
│  **Purpose**                | Scale reads           | High availability     │
│  **Replication**            | Asynchronous          | Synchronous           │
│  **Can handle writes?**     | No (read-only)        | No (standby, but      │
│                            |                       | can't write)          │
│  **Number allowed**         | Up to 5 (or cascade)  | Only 1 standby        │
│  **Failover**               | Manual (promote)      | Automatic (30-60 sec) │
│  **Data loss on failover**  | Possible (async)      | None (sync)           │
│  **Performance impact**     | Minimal on primary    | Some (sync commit)    │
│  **Cross-region?**          | Yes                   | No (same region)      │
│  **Cost**                   | Additional instance   | Additional instance   │
│                                                                             │
│  When to use which:                                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Use Read Replicas when:                                            │   │
│  │  - Read-heavy workload (80%+ reads)                                 │   │
│  │  - Need global read distribution                                    │   │
│  │  - Can tolerate some lag (<1 second usually)                        │   │
│  │  - Want to offload reporting/analytics                              │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Use Multi-AZ when:                                                 │   │
│  │  - Need automatic failover (high availability)                      │   │
│  │  - Cannot lose any data (RPO = 0)                                   │   │
│  │  - Write-heavy workload                                             │   │
│  │  - Can't tolerate lag                                               │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  BEST PRACTICE: Use BOTH!                                           │   │
│  │  - Multi-AZ for automatic failover                                  │   │
│  │  - Read replicas for scaling reads                                  │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 5. Implementation Example (Application Code)

```java
// Spring Boot Application with Read Replica Support

@Configuration
public class DatabaseConfig {
    
    @Bean
    @Primary
    @ConfigurationProperties(prefix = "spring.datasource.primary")
    public DataSource primaryDataSource() {
        // For writes - points to primary RDS instance
        return DataSourceBuilder.create()
            .url("jdbc:postgresql://my-primary.xxx.us-east-1.rds.amazonaws.com:5432/mydb")
            .username("admin")
            .password("${DB_PASSWORD}")
            .build();
    }
    
    @Bean
    @ConfigurationProperties(prefix = "spring.datasource.replica")
    public DataSource replicaDataSource() {
        // For reads - points to reader endpoint (load balancer across replicas)
        return DataSourceBuilder.create()
            .url("jdbc:postgresql://my-reader-endpoint.xxx.us-east-1.rds.amazonaws.com:5432/mydb")
            .username("readonly")
            .password("${READONLY_PASSWORD}")
            .build();
    }
    
    @Bean
    public DataSource routingDataSource() {
        RoutingDataSource routingDataSource = new RoutingDataSource();
        
        Map<Object, Object> targetDataSources = new HashMap<>();
        targetDataSources.put("write", primaryDataSource());
        targetDataSources.put("read", replicaDataSource());
        
        routingDataSource.setTargetDataSources(targetDataSources);
        routingDataSource.setDefaultTargetDataSource(primaryDataSource());
        
        return routingDataSource;
    }
}

// Using @Transactional to route reads vs writes
@Service
public class UserService {
    
    @Autowired
    private UserRepository userRepository;
    
    // Write operation - uses primary
    @Transactional
    public User createUser(User user) {
        return userRepository.save(user);
    }
    
    // Read operation - can use replica
    @Transactional(readOnly = true)
    public User getUser(Long id) {
        return userRepository.findById(id).orElse(null);
    }
}
```

### 6. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"Read replicas are for scaling read-heavy workloads. In one project, we had 90% reads and 10% writes. We added 3 read replicas and used a reader endpoint. Read latency dropped from 50ms to 10ms. We also used a separate reporting replica for analytics queries so they wouldn't affect production. The key trade-off is that replication is asynchronous, so there's eventual consistency. For critical reads where consistency matters, we still read from primary."*

**Key points to mention:**

1. **Asynchronous replication** - No performance impact on primary
2. **Read scaling** - Offload SELECT queries
3. **Eventual consistency** - Replica lag exists
4. **Can be promoted** - For disaster recovery
5. **Different AZs/regions** - For HA and global distribution

### 7. Short Summary

```
Read Replicas - Quick Reference:

Purpose: Scale read traffic, offload primary
Replication: Asynchronous (non-blocking)
Lag: Typically <100ms (can spike)
Max replicas: 5 direct (cascade for more)

Use Cases:
✅ Read-heavy applications (80%+ reads)
✅ Reporting/analytics (isolate workload)
✅ Global read distribution
✅ Disaster recovery (can promote)

Not For:
❌ Write scaling (use sharding)
❌ Strong consistency requirements
❌ Real-time critical reads

Best Practice:
Multi-AZ + Read Replicas = HA + Performance

Interview Hook:
"Read replicas are for read scaling. 
But remember - they're eventually consistent. 
For critical reads where accuracy matters, still use primary."
```

---

## ❓ Q13. How do you handle DB scaling?

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
Database scaling = Database ko **badhte traffic** ke saath handle karne ke liye **upgrade** ya **distribute** karna.

**Intermediate:**  
DB scaling has two dimensions:
- **Vertical scaling** (bigger instance) - Limited, has ceiling
- **Horizontal scaling** (more instances/servers) - Unlimited but complex

**Advanced (Scaling Pyramid):**

```
Database Scaling Strategies (From Simple to Complex):

Level 1: Vertical Scaling (Scale Up)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ t3.micro (1GB) → t3.large (8GB) → r5.4xlarge (64GB)       │
│                                                             │
│ Pros: Simple, no app changes                               │
│ Cons: Expensive, has limit (max 64TB, 448 vCPU)           │
│ When: Early stage, low to medium traffic                   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Level 2: Read Replicas
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Primary (writes) + 5 Read Replicas (reads)                 │
│                                                             │
│ Pros: Scales reads, simple                                 │
│ Cons: Doesn't scale writes                                 │
│ When: Read-heavy workload (80%+ reads)                     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Level 3: Caching Layer
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ App → Redis Cache (90% hits) → DB (10% misses)             │
│                                                             │
│ Pros: Reduces DB load dramatically                         │
│ Cons: Cache invalidation complexity                        │
│ When: Repeatable read patterns                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Level 4: Database Sharding (Horizontal Partitioning)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Shard 1 (users 0-1M)   Shard 2 (users 1M-2M)   Shard 3    │
│                                                             │
│ Pros: Scales writes, unlimited                             │
│ Cons: Complex, no joins across shards                      │
│ When: Very high write throughput, huge dataset             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Level 5: Database Migration (Different DB Type)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ RDS (SQL) → DynamoDB (NoSQL)                               │
│                                                             │
│ Pros: Massive scale, lower latency                         │
│ Cons: Redesign application, lose SQL features              │
│ When: SQL limitations reached                              │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Detailed Scaling Strategies

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    DATABASE SCALING STRATEGIES - DEEP DIVE                  │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 1: Vertical Scaling (Scale Up)                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  RDS Instance Types (2024):                                         │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  Instance    | vCPU | RAM    | Max IOPS | Use Case          │    │   │
│  │  │  ────────────┼──────┼────────┼──────────┼──────────────────│    │   │
│  │  │  db.t4g.micro| 2    | 1GB    | 2,500    | Dev/Test          │    │   │
│  │  │  db.t4g.large| 2    | 8GB    | 5,000    | Small production  │    │   │
│  │  │  db.r5.large | 2    | 16GB   | 16,000   | Standard          │    │   │
│  │  │  db.r5.4xlarge|16   | 128GB  | 64,000   | High traffic      │    │   │
│  │  │  db.r5.12xlarge|48 | 384GB  | 80,000   | Very high         │    │   │
│  │  │  db.r5.24xlarge|96 | 768GB  | 160,000  | Max (vertical)    │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  When to Scale Up:                                                   │   │
│  │  - CPU consistently > 70%                                           │   │
│  │  - Memory pressure (swap usage)                                     │   │
│  │  - IOPS limit reached                                               │   │
│  │  - Connection limit reached                                         │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Downtime: 5-15 minutes (varies by engine)                          │   │
│  │  Cost: Increases linearly (2x RAM = 2x cost)                        │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 2: Read Replicas (Scale Reads)                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Implementation:                                                    │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  Application changes:                                        │    │   │
│  │  │  - Write queries: Primary endpoint                          │    │   │
│  │  │  - Read queries: Reader endpoint (load balancer)            │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  @Transactional(readOnly = true)  // Routes to replica      │    │   │
│  │  │  public List<User> getUsers() { ... }                       │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Limits:                                                            │   │
│  │  - Max 5 direct replicas (can cascade for more)                    │   │
│  │  - Replica lag (usually <100ms, can spike)                         │   │
│  │  - Doesn't scale writes                                             │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Best for: Read-heavy (90% reads, 10% writes)                      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 3: Caching (Reduce DB Load)                                      │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Cache Patterns:                                                    │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  1. Cache-Aside (Lazy Loading):                            │    │   │
│  │  │     Read: Check cache → Miss → Read DB → Store in cache    │    │   │
│  │  │     Write: Write DB → Invalidate cache                     │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  2. Write-Through:                                         │    │   │
│  │  │     Write: Write DB AND cache together                     │    │   │
│  │  │     Read: Always from cache                                │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  3. Write-Behind:                                          │    │   │
│  │  │     Write: Write to cache only → Async write to DB         │    │   │
│  │  │     (Risk of data loss)                                    │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Cache Hit Ratio Targets:                                           │   │
│  │  - Session data: 99%+                                              │   │
│  │  - Product catalog: 95%+                                           │   │
│  │  - User profiles: 90%+                                             │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Technology: ElastiCache Redis (sub-millisecond latency)           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 4: Database Sharding (Horizontal Scaling)                       │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Sharding Architecture:                                             │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  │  Application                                                │    │   │
│  │  │      │                                                      │    │   │
│  │  │      ▼                                                      │    │   │
│  │  │  Sharding Layer (Consistent Hashing)                        │    │   │
│  │  │      │                                                      │    │   │
│  │  │      ├──────────┬──────────┬──────────┐                    │    │   │
│  │  │      ▼          ▼          ▼          ▼                    │    │   │
│  │  │  Shard 1    Shard 2    Shard 3    Shard 4                  │    │   │
│  │  │  (users     (users     (users     (users                   │    │   │
│  │  │   0-25M)     25M-50M)   50M-75M)   75M-100M)               │    │   │
│  │  │                                                             │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Sharding Key Selection:                                            │   │
│  │  - user_id (good for user-centric apps)                            │   │
│  │  - order_id (good for order-centric apps)                          │   │
│  │  - tenant_id (for multi-tenant SaaS)                               │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Challenges:                                                        │   │
│  │  - Cross-shard queries impossible (no JOINs)                       │   │
│  │  - Rebalancing (adding new shards) is complex                      │   │
│  │  - Transaction across shards (use 2PC or Saga)                     │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  AWS Solutions:                                                    │   │
│  │  - Aurora Limitless Database (automatic sharding)                  │   │
│  │  - DynamoDB (automatic sharding)                                   │   │
│  │  - Vitess (open source, runs on RDS)                               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  STRATEGY 5: Database Migration (SQL → NoSQL)                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  When to migrate:                                                   │   │
│  │  - RDS vertical limit reached (768GB RAM, 64TB storage)             │   │
│  │  - Write throughput exceeds RDS capabilities (>100K writes/sec)    │   │
│  │  - Need auto-scaling for spiky traffic                              │   │
│  │  - Access patterns are simple (mostly key-value)                    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Migration Path:                                                    │   │
│  │  1. Dual-write (write to both RDS and DynamoDB)                    │   │
│  │  2. Backfill historical data                                        │   │
│  │  3. Verify data consistency                                         │   │
│  │  4. Switch reads to DynamoDB                                        │   │
│  │  5. Remove RDS                                                      │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Tools: AWS DMS (Database Migration Service)                        │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Real-World Scaling Journey (Example)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    REAL-WORLD SCALING JOURNEY                               │
│                    (E-commerce Platform)                                    │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Phase 1: 0-10,000 users                                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Solution: Single RDS db.t3.large                                   │   │
│  │  Traffic: 100 req/sec, 50/50 read/write                            │   │
│  │  Issues: None                                                        │   │
│  │  Cost: $150/month                                                   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Phase 2: 10,000 - 100,000 users                                           │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Problem: Read traffic increasing (80% reads)                       │   │
│  │  Solution: Add 2 read replicas + Redis cache                        │   │
│  │  Traffic: 1,000 req/sec, 80% reads                                  │   │
│  │  Result: Primary CPU 30%, replicas 60%                              │   │
│  │  Cost: $400/month                                                   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Phase 3: 100,000 - 1,000,000 users                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Problem: Write traffic growing (50K writes/sec)                    │   │
│  │  Solution: Vertical scale to db.r5.4xlarge (16 vCPU, 128GB)         │   │
│  │  Traffic: 10,000 req/sec, 60% reads                                 │   │
│  │  Result: Primary CPU 70% (near limit)                               │   │
│  │  Cost: $1,500/month                                                 │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Phase 4: 1,000,000 - 10,000,000 users                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Problem: Vertical limit reached (max RDS instance)                 │   │
│  │  Solution: Shard by user_id across 8 RDS instances                  │   │
│  │  Traffic: 100,000 req/sec                                           │   │
│  │  Result: Each shard handles 12,500 req/sec                          │   │
│  │  Cost: $8,000/month                                                 │   │
│  │  Complexity: High (app redesign needed)                             │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Phase 5: 10,000,000+ users                                                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Problem: Sharding complexity, need auto-scaling                    │   │
│  │  Solution: Migrate to DynamoDB (auto-sharding)                      │   │
│  │  Traffic: 1,000,000 req/sec                                         │   │
│  │  Result: Handles automatically, no manual sharding                  │   │
│  │  Cost: $30,000/month (but cheaper than managing 50 RDS shards)      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4. Decision Framework

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              DATABASE SCALING DECISION TREE                                 │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Question 1: Is CPU/Memory > 70%?                                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  YES → Vertical scaling (bigger instance)                           │   │
│  │  NO  → Continue                                                     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Question 2: Is read traffic > write traffic?                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  YES (80%+ reads) → Add read replicas                               │   │
│  │  NO → Continue                                                      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Question 3: Are there repeatable queries?                                 │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  YES → Add caching layer (Redis)                                    │   │
│  │  NO  → Continue                                                     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Question 4: Is write throughput still too high?                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  YES → Sharding (horizontal partition)                              │   │
│  │  NO  → Continue                                                     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Question 5: Is sharding too complex?                                      │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  YES → Consider DynamoDB (auto-sharding)                            │   │
│  │  NO  → Implement sharding on RDS                                    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 5. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"Database scaling is a journey. I start with vertical scaling - it's simple and works for a long time. When read traffic grows, I add read replicas. I always add caching early - Redis reduces DB load by 80-90%. When writes become the bottleneck, I consider sharding. But sharding is complex - no cross-shard joins, transactions become hard. At that point, I evaluate if DynamoDB's auto-sharding might be a better fit. The key is to scale incrementally and not over-engineer too early."*

**Key points to mention:**

1. **Start simple** - Vertical scaling first
2. **Read replicas** - For read-heavy workloads
3. **Cache aggressively** - Biggest impact
4. **Sharding as last resort** - Complex but powerful
5. **Consider NoSQL** - If access patterns fit

### 6. Short Summary

```
Database Scaling - Quick Reference:

Scaling Strategies (Simple → Complex):

1. Vertical Scaling (Scale Up)
   - Bigger instance
   - Simple, no code changes
   - Limit: Max instance size

2. Read Replicas
   - Offload SELECT queries
   - Simple, code changes needed
   - Limit: Doesn't scale writes

3. Caching (Redis)
   - Reduce DB load 80-90%
   - Medium complexity
   - Limit: Cache invalidation

4. Sharding (Horizontal)
   - Partition data across DBs
   - High complexity
   - Limit: No cross-shard operations

5. NoSQL Migration
   - DynamoDB auto-sharding
   - Very high complexity
   - Limit: Lose SQL features

Best Practice:
Cache first, read replicas second, 
vertical scaling third, sharding last.

Interview Hook:
"Database scaling is about buying time. 
Caching buys you the most time with the least effort. 
Only shard when you absolutely have to."
```

- Monitoring (CloudWatch, X-Ray)
