# 🔁 7. MESSAGING & ASYNC SYSTEMS

## ❓ Q21. What is SQS?

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
SQS = Simple Queue Service. Ek **message queue** hai jahan ek service message daal sakti hai, aur doosri service baad mein padh sakti hai. **Decoupling** ke liye use hota hai.

**Intermediate:**  
SQS = Fully managed **message queue** for decoupling application components. Supports **at-least-once** delivery, **automatic scaling**, and **dead-letter queues** for failed messages.

**Advanced (Internal Working):**

```
SQS Internal Architecture:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  PRODUCER (sends messages)                                                 │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Order Service ──→ SendMessage() ──→ {"orderId": "123"}             │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    SQS Queue (Distributed)                          │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │  Messages stored across multiple AZs (redundant)            │   │   │
│  │  │                                                              │   │   │
│  │  │  [Msg1] ──→ [Msg2] ──→ [Msg3] ──→ [Msg4] ──→ [Msg5]        │   │   │
│  │  │    ↑           ↑           ↑           ↑           ↑         │   │   │
│  │  │  Visible     Visible     Visible     Visible     Visible      │   │   │
│  │  │                                                              │   │   │
│  │  │  Retention: 4 days (default) to 14 days (max)               │   │   │
│  │  │  Visibility timeout: 30 seconds (default)                   │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  CONSUMER (receives messages)                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Payment Service ──→ ReceiveMessage() ──→ gets Msg1                 │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Step 1: Receive message (becomes invisible)                        │   │
│  │  Step 2: Process message (payment)                                  │   │
│  │  Step 3: DeleteMessage() (removes from queue)                       │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  If processing fails → message reappears after visibility timeout   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. SQS Queue Types & Features

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    SQS QUEUE TYPES & FEATURES                               │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  QUEUE TYPE 1: Standard Queue                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Features:                                                           │   │
│  │  - Unlimited throughput (millions of messages/sec)                  │   │
│  │  - At-least-once delivery (may get duplicates)                      │   │
│  │  - Best-effort ordering (not guaranteed)                            │   │
│  │  - Lower latency                                                    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Use Case: Order processing, background jobs, decoupling            │   │
│  │  (Most common, use this unless you need FIFO)                       │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  QUEUE TYPE 2: FIFO Queue (First-In-First-Out)                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Features:                                                           │   │
│  │  - Exactly-once processing (no duplicates)                          │   │
│  │  - Guaranteed ordering                                              │   │
│  │  - Limited throughput: 300 messages/sec (3,000 with batching)       │   │
│  │  - Higher latency                                                   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Use Case: Banking transactions, inventory updates, any order-      │   │
│  │  sensitive operations                                               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  KEY FEATURES:                                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  1. Visibility Timeout                                             │   │
│  │     - How long message is invisible after being read               │   │
│  │     - Default: 30 seconds                                          │   │
│  │     - Increase if processing takes longer                          │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  2. Dead Letter Queue (DLQ)                                        │   │
│  │     - Messages that fail processing go here                        │   │
│  │     - Max receives: 3 (configurable)                               │   │
│  │     - Prevents poison messages from blocking queue                 │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  3. Delay Queue                                                     │   │
│  │     - Messages become visible after delay                          │   │
│  │     - Example: Retry with backoff                                  │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  4. Long Polling                                                    │   │
│  │     - Consumer waits for messages (up to 20 seconds)               │   │
│  │     - Reduces empty responses (reduces cost)                       │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  5. Message Size                                                    │   │
│  │     - Max 256KB per message                                        │   │
│  │     - For larger: Store in S3, send reference                      │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  6. Retention Period                                                │   │
│  │     - 4 days (default) to 14 days (max)                            │   │
│  │     - Messages deleted after retention                             │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. SQS Implementation Examples

```java
// Spring Boot SQS Producer
@Service
public class OrderProducer {
    
    private final AmazonSQS sqsClient;
    private final String queueUrl = "https://sqs.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/123456789012/orders-queue";
    
    public void sendOrder(Order order) {
        SendMessageRequest request = new SendMessageRequest()
            .withQueueUrl(queueUrl)
            .withMessageBody(order.toJson())
            .withDelaySeconds(0)  // No delay
            .withMessageAttributes(Map.of(
                "OrderType", new MessageAttributeValue()
                    .withDataType("String")
                    .withStringValue(order.getType())
            ));
        
        sqsClient.sendMessage(request);
    }
}

// Spring Boot SQS Consumer
@Component
public class OrderConsumer {
    
    private final AmazonSQS sqsClient;
    private final String queueUrl;
    
    @Scheduled(fixedDelay = 5000)  // Poll every 5 seconds
    public void pollMessages() {
        ReceiveMessageRequest request = new ReceiveMessageRequest()
            .withQueueUrl(queueUrl)
            .withMaxNumberOfMessages(10)  // Batch size
            .withWaitTimeSeconds(20)       // Long polling
            .withVisibilityTimeout(60);    // 60 seconds to process
        
        List<Message> messages = sqsClient.receiveMessage(request).getMessages();
        
        for (Message message : messages) {
            try {
                // Process order
                Order order = Order.fromJson(message.getBody());
                processOrder(order);
                
                // Delete after successful processing
                sqsClient.deleteMessage(queueUrl, message.getReceiptHandle());
            } catch (Exception e) {
                // Message will reappear after visibility timeout
                log.error("Failed to process order", e);
            }
        }
    }
}

// Using Spring Cloud AWS (Simpler)
@Configuration
public class SqsConfig {
    
    @Bean
    public QueueMessageHandlerFactory queueMessageHandlerFactory() {
        QueueMessageHandlerFactory factory = new QueueMessageHandlerFactory();
        factory.setQueueMessageHandlerMethodFactory(new QueueMessageHandlerMethodFactory());
        return factory;
    }
}

@Component
public class SqsListener {
    
    @SqsListener(value = "orders-queue", deletionPolicy = SqsMessageDeletionPolicy.ON_SUCCESS)
    public void handleOrder(String message, @Header("SenderId") String senderId) {
        // Automatically deleted if no exception
        Order order = new ObjectMapper().readValue(message, Order.class);
        processOrder(order);
    }
}
```

### 4. Common Patterns

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    SQS COMMON PATTERNS                                      │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN 1: Load Leveling (Smooth out traffic spikes)                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Spiky Traffic:              SQS Queue:        Smooth Processing:   │   │
│  │  ┌─────┐                     ┌─────┐           ┌─────┐              │   │
│  │  │10K  │────────────────────→│████│───────────→│1K   │              │   │
│  │  │req/s│                     │████│           │req/s│              │   │
│  │  └─────┘                     │████│           └─────┘              │   │
│  │                              └─────┘                                │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Benefit: Backend never overloaded, processes at its own pace       │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN 2: Decoupling Microservices                                       │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Order Service ──→ SQS ──→ Payment Service                         │   │
│  │                   │                                                 │   │
│  │                   └──→ SQS ──→ Inventory Service                    │   │
│  │                   │                                                 │   │
│  │                   └──→ SQS ──→ Email Service                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Benefit: Services don't need to know about each other              │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN 3: Dead Letter Queue (Error Handling)                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Main Queue ──(3 failed attempts)──→ Dead Letter Queue              │   │
│  │      │                                        │                       │   │
│  │      │                                        ▼                       │   │
│  │   Processing                           Alert: Manual review          │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Benefit: Failed messages don't block queue, can be analyzed later   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN 4: Retry with Exponential Backoff                                 │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Attempt 1: Fail → Visibility timeout = 1 second                    │   │
│  │  Attempt 2: Fail → Visibility timeout = 2 seconds                   │   │
│  │  Attempt 3: Fail → Visibility timeout = 4 seconds                   │   │
│  │  Attempt 4: Fail → Send to DLQ                                      │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Benefit: Gives external dependencies time to recover               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 5. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"SQS is our go-to for decoupling services. For example, when an order is placed, the order service sends a message to SQS and returns immediately. The payment service polls the queue and processes payments at its own pace. This handles traffic spikes because the queue acts as a buffer. We use standard queues for most cases because throughput is unlimited. For critical operations like inventory updates where order matters, we use FIFO queues. We always configure a dead letter queue - after 3 failed attempts, messages go to DLQ for manual inspection."*

**Key points to mention:**

1. **Decoupling** - Services don't need to know about each other
2. **Buffering** - Handles traffic spikes
3. **At-least-once** - Be prepared for duplicates (make idempotent)
4. **DLQ** - Always configure for failed messages
5. **Long polling** - Reduces cost and latency

---

## ❓ Q22. SQS vs SNS

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
- **SQS** = Queue (one consumer reads each message)
- **SNS** = Pub-Sub (all subscribers get each message)

**Advanced (Complete Comparison):**

```
SQS vs SNS - VISUAL COMPARISON:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  SQS (Queue - Point to Point):                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Producer ──→ SQS Queue ──→ Consumer A (reads message)              │   │
│  │                           ──→ Consumer B (does NOT see it)           │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  One message, one consumer (load balancing)                          │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  SNS (Pub-Sub - Fan-out):                                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │                    ┌─→ SQS Queue A ──→ Consumer A                   │   │
│  │                    │                                                │   │
│  │  Producer ──→ SNS Topic ──┼─→ SQS Queue B ──→ Consumer B            │   │
│  │                    │                                                │   │
│  │                    └─→ Lambda Function C ──→ Process                │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  One message, multiple subscribers (broadcasting)                    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Detailed Comparison Table

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    SQS vs SNS - COMPLETE COMPARISON                         │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Feature              | SQS                    | SNS                        │
│  ─────────────────────┼────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────│
│  **Model**            | Point-to-point (Queue) | Publish-Subscribe (Topic) │
│  **Consumers**        | One consumer per       | All subscribers get copy  │
│                       | message                |                           │
│  **Delivery**         | Pull-based (poll)      | Push-based (to endpoints) │
│  **Persistence**      | Yes (4-14 days)        | No (not persisted)        │
│  **Retry**            | Consumer handles       | SNS retries (3 times)     │
│  **Filtering**        | No                     | Yes (message filtering)   │
│  **Ordering**         | FIFO queues available  | No ordering guarantee     │
│  **Duplicate messages**| Possible (standard)    | Possible                   │
│  **Use Case**         | Decoupling, load       | Broadcasting, fan-out     │
│                       | leveling               |                           │
│                                                                             │
│  Subscriber Types (SNS):                                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  - SQS Queue (most common)                                          │   │
│  │  - Lambda Function                                                  │   │
│  │  - HTTP/HTTPS Endpoint                                              │   │
│  │  - Email (SMS)                                                      │   │
│  │  - Mobile Push                                                      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Real-World Patterns (SQS + SNS Together)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    SQS + SNS TOGETHER (Fan-out Pattern)                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  PATTERN: Order Created Event - Fan-out to multiple services               │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Order Service                                                       │   │
│  │      │                                                               │   │
│  │      │ Publish to SNS Topic "order-created"                         │   │
│  │      ▼                                                               │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │                    SNS Topic                                 │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │      │                    │                    │                    │   │
│  │      │ (subscription)     │ (subscription)     │ (subscription)     │   │
│  │      ▼                    ▼                    ▼                    │   │
│  │  ┌─────────┐          ┌─────────┐          ┌─────────┐             │   │
│  │  │ SQS A   │          │ SQS B   │          │ SQS C   │             │   │
│  │  │(Payment)│          │(Inventory)│         │(Email)  │             │   │
│  │  └────┬────┘          └────┬────┘          └────┬────┘             │   │
│  │       │                    │                    │                    │   │
│  │       ▼                    ▼                    ▼                    │   │
│  │  Payment Service      Inventory Service     Email Service           │   │
│  │  (process payment)    (update stock)       (send confirmation)     │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Benefits:                                                          │   │
│  │  - Each service works independently                                 │   │
│  │  - If email service is down, payment still processes               │   │
│  │  - New services can subscribe without changing order service       │   │
│  │  - SQS buffers messages if any service is slow                     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4. Implementation Examples

```java
// SNS Publisher
@Service
public class OrderEventPublisher {
    
    private final AmazonSNS snsClient;
    private final String topicArn = "arn:aws:sns:us-east-1:123456789012:order-created";
    
    public void publishOrderCreated(Order order) {
        PublishRequest request = new PublishRequest()
            .withTopicArn(topicArn)
            .withMessage(order.toJson())
            .withMessageAttributes(Map.of(
                "eventType", new MessageAttributeValue()
                    .withDataType("String")
                    .withStringValue("ORDER_CREATED")
            ));
        
        snsClient.publish(request);
    }
}

// SQS Consumer (subscribed to SNS)
@Component
public class PaymentConsumer {
    
    @SqsListener("payment-queue")
    public void handleOrder(Order order) {
        // This message came from SNS via SQS
        processPayment(order);
    }
}

// Using SNS + SQS together (best practice)
@Configuration
public class SnsSqsConfig {
    
    @Bean
    public SNSClient snsClient() {
        return SNSClient.builder().build();
    }
    
    @Bean
    public SqsAsyncClient sqsClient() {
        return SqsAsyncClient.builder().build();
    }
    
    // Subscribe SQS to SNS automatically
    @Bean
    public CommandLineRunner subscribeQueueToTopic(
            SNSClient sns, SqsAsyncClient sqs) {
        return args -> {
            String queueArn = sqs.getQueueAttributes(b -> b.queueUrl("https://...").attributeNames("QueueArn"))
                .get().attributes().get("QueueArn");
            
            sns.subscribe(b -> b
                .topicArn("arn:aws:sns:...")
                .protocol("sqs")
                .endpoint(queueArn));
        };
    }
}
```

### 5. Decision Framework

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              SQS vs SNS - WHEN TO USE WHICH?                                │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Use SQS When:                                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  ✅ You need to decouple two services                               │   │
│  │  ✅ You want load leveling (buffer spikes)                          │   │
│  │  ✅ Only one service needs to process each message                  │   │
│  │  ✅ You need message persistence (4-14 days)                        │   │
│  │  ✅ Example: Order Service → Queue → Payment Service                │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Use SNS When:                                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  ✅ You need to broadcast to multiple subscribers                   │   │
│  │  ✅ New services can subscribe without changing publisher           │   │
│  │  ✅ You need message filtering (different subscribers get different │   │
│  │     messages based on attributes)                                   │   │
│  │  ✅ Example: Order Created → Notify Payment, Inventory, Email       │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Use BOTH (SNS → SQS) When:                                                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  ✅ You need fan-out + buffering + persistence                      │   │
│  │  ✅ Each subscriber can process at its own pace                     │   │
│  │  ✅ If a subscriber is down, messages are queued                    │   │
│  │  ✅ Most common pattern in production!                              │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 6. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"SQS is for point-to-point messaging where one consumer processes each message. SNS is for pub-sub where multiple subscribers get each message. In production, we often use them together - publish to SNS, which fans out to multiple SQS queues. This gives us the best of both worlds: each subscriber gets its own queue for buffering and retries, and new subscribers can be added without changing the publisher. For example, when an order is created, we publish to SNS. The payment service, inventory service, and email service each have their own SQS queue subscribed to that SNS topic."*

### 7. Short Summary

```
SQS vs SNS - Quick Reference:

SQS (Queue):
- One message, one consumer
- Pull-based (consumer polls)
- Persistence (4-14 days)
- Use for: Decoupling, load leveling

SNS (Topic):
- One message, many subscribers
- Push-based (SNS pushes)
- No persistence
- Use for: Broadcasting, fan-out

Best Practice: SNS → SQS
- Fan-out + buffering + persistence
- Each subscriber gets its own queue
- Most production pattern

Interview Hook:
"SQS is for work distribution, SNS is for event broadcast. 
Use SNS→SQS when you need both - it's the standard pattern 
for event-driven architectures on AWS."
```

---

## ❓ Q23. Event-driven architecture in AWS

### 1. Concept Explanation (Beginner → Advanced)

**Beginner:**  
Event-driven = Services **directly call** nahi karte. Balki **events** publish karte hain. Doosre services **react** karte hain jab event aata hai.

**Advanced (Complete Event-Driven Architecture):**

```
EVENT-DRIVEN ARCHITECTURE - COMPLETE DIAGRAM:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  EVENT SOURCES:                                                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  User Action ──→ API Gateway ──→ Lambda (publishes event)           │   │
│  │  Database Change ──→ DynamoDB Streams ──→ Event                     │   │
│  │  File Upload ──→ S3 Event Notification ──→ Event                    │   │
│  │  Scheduled Time ──→ EventBridge (cron) ──→ Event                    │   │
│  │  Service Action ──→ SNS / EventBridge ──→ Event                     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    EVENT BUS (Router)                               │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │  Amazon EventBridge (recommended for modern apps)           │   │   │
│  │  │  - Event routing with rules                                 │   │   │
│  │  │  - Schema registry                                          │   │   │
│  │  │  - SaaS integrations (Shopify, Zendesk, etc.)               │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  OR SNS (simpler, less features)                                    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  EVENT CONSUMERS (React to events):                                       │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Event ──┬──→ Lambda (process) ──→ Update Database                  │   │
│  │          ├──→ SQS Queue (buffer) ──→ EC2 Worker                     │   │
│  │          ├──→ Step Functions (orchestrate)                          │   │
│  │          ├──→ SNS (notify users)                                    │   │
│  │          └──→ Kinesis (stream to analytics)                         │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Complete Event-Driven Example (E-commerce)

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         EVENT-DRIVEN E-COMMERCE ARCHITECTURE (Real Example)                 │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  EVENT: "Order Placed"                                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Order Service ──→ EventBridge ──→ Rule: event.type = "order.placed"│   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    PARALLEL EVENT HANDLERS                           │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │ Handler 1: Payment Processing                                │   │   │
│  │  │ EventBridge → SQS (payment-queue) → Lambda → Payment API     │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │ Handler 2: Inventory Update                                  │   │   │
│  │  │ EventBridge → Lambda → Update DynamoDB (inventory)          │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │ Handler 3: Email Notification                                │   │   │
│  │  │ EventBridge → SQS (email-queue) → Lambda → SES              │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │ Handler 4: Analytics                                        │   │   │
│  │  │ EventBridge → Kinesis → Redshift (real-time dashboard)     │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │ Handler 5: Fraud Detection (async)                           │   │   │
│  │  │ EventBridge → SQS → Lambda → ML Model                       │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Benefits:                                                                 │
│  - Order service doesn't know about payment, inventory, email, analytics   │
│  - New handlers can be added without changing order service               │
│  - If email service fails, order is still processed                       │
│  - Each handler can scale independently                                    │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. EventBridge vs SNS

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    EVENTBRIDGE vs SNS - COMPLETE COMPARISON                 │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Feature              | EventBridge            | SNS                        │
│  ─────────────────────┼────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────│
│  **Complex routing**  | Yes (rules with       | No (all subscribers get   │
│                       | filtering)             | all messages)            │
│  **Schema registry**  | Yes                    | No                         │
│  **SaaS integrations**| Yes (200+ services)   | No (custom only)          │
│  **Transform events** | Yes (input transformer)| No                         │
│  **Archive/replay**   | Yes (replay old events)| No                         │
│  **Targets**          | 20+ targets (Lambda,   | Limited (SQS, Lambda,    │
│                       | SQS, Step Functions,   | HTTP, Email)             │
│                       | Kinesis, etc.)         |                           │
│  **Use Case**         | Modern event-driven    | Simple pub-sub           │
│                       | architectures          |                           │
│                                                                             │
│  When to use EventBridge:                                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  ✅ Complex routing (different targets for different events)        │   │
│  │  ✅ Need event transformation                                        │   │
│  │  ✅ Need to replay events                                            │   │
│  │  ✅ Integrating with SaaS apps (Salesforce, Zendesk, etc.)          │   │
│  │  ✅ Modern event-driven architecture                                 │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  When to use SNS:                                                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  ✅ Simple fan-out (all subscribers get everything)                 │   │
│  │  ✅ Need mobile push notifications                                   │   │
│  │  ✅ Need SMS/email delivery                                          │   │
│  │  ✅ Simpler setup                                                   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4. EventBridge Implementation Example

```java
// Publishing event to EventBridge
@Service
public class EventPublisher {
    
    private final EventBridgeClient eventBridge;
    
    public void publishOrderPlaced(Order order) {
        
        // Create event
        EventBridgeEvent event = EventBridgeEvent.builder()
            .source("com.myapp.order-service")
            .detailType("OrderPlaced")
            .time(Instant.now())
            .detail(order.toJson())
            .resources(List.of("order-service-prod"))
            .build();
        
        // Put events
        PutEventsRequestEntry entry = PutEventsRequestEntry.builder()
            .eventBusName("default")
            .source(event.getSource())
            .detailType(event.getDetailType())
            .time(event.getTime())
            .detail(event.getDetail())
            .build();
        
        PutEventsRequest request = PutEventsRequest.builder()
            .entries(entry)
            .build();
        
        eventBridge.putEvents(request);
    }
}

// EventBridge Rule (via CloudFormation)
Resources:
  OrderPlacedRule:
    Type: AWS::Events::Rule
    Properties:
      EventBusName: default
      EventPattern:
        source:
          - "com.myapp.order-service"
        detail-type:
          - "OrderPlaced"
      Targets:
        - Arn: !GetAtt PaymentQueue.Arn
          Id: PaymentTarget
        - Arn: !GetAtt InventoryLambda.Arn
          Id: InventoryTarget

// Consumer (Lambda triggered by EventBridge)
public class OrderEventHandler implements RequestHandler<EventBridgeEvent, Void> {
    
    @Override
    public Void handleRequest(EventBridgeEvent event, Context context) {
        String detailType = event.getDetailType();
        String detail = event.getDetail();
        
        switch (detailType) {
            case "OrderPlaced":
                Order order = parseOrder(detail);
                processOrder(order);
                break;
            case "PaymentProcessed":
                Payment payment = parsePayment(detail);
                updateOrderStatus(payment);
                break;
        }
        return null;
    }
}
```

### 5. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"Event-driven architecture is the foundation of scalable microservices. Instead of services calling each other directly, they publish events to EventBridge. For example, when an order is placed, the order service just publishes an 'OrderPlaced' event. Payment, inventory, email, and analytics services all subscribe to this event. This completely decouples the services - if email is down, orders still get processed. New services can be added without changing existing ones. We use EventBridge because it supports complex routing, event transformation, and can replay events if needed."*

**Key points to mention:**

1. **Decoupling** - Services don't know about each other
2. **Resilience** - One service failing doesn't affect others
3. **Scalability** - Each service scales independently
4. **Extensibility** - Add new subscribers without changes
5. **EventBridge** - Modern approach with routing and replay

### 6. Short Summary

```
Event-Driven Architecture - Quick Reference:

Core Components:
1. Event Source (produces events)
2. Event Bus (routes events - EventBridge/SNS)
3. Event Consumers (react to events)

Benefits:
- Loose coupling
- Resilience (failure isolation)
- Independent scaling
- Easy to extend

AWS Services:
- EventBridge (recommended for modern apps)
- SNS (simpler fan-out)
- SQS (buffering for consumers)
- DynamoDB Streams (DB change events)
- S3 Events (file upload events)

Pattern:
Event Source → EventBridge → Rules → Targets (SQS/Lambda)

Interview Hook:
"Event-driven is the default for microservices. 
Instead of REST calls between services, they publish events. 
This makes the system more resilient, scalable, and maintainable."
```

# 🧠 8. SCENARIO-BASED QUESTIONS (Very Important)

## ❓ Q24. Your API is slow, how will you optimize?

### 1. Systematic Debugging Approach

```
SLOW API - SYSTEMATIC DEBUGGING FLOWCHART:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  START: User reports "API is slow"                                          │
│       │                                                                     │
│       ▼                                                                     │
│  STEP 1: MEASURE (Don't guess, measure!)                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  - Check CloudWatch metrics (latency p50, p90, p99)                  │   │
│  │  - Check X-Ray traces (which component is slow?)                    │   │
│  │  - Check API Gateway/ALB access logs                                │   │
│  │  - Reproduce with curl + time                                        │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│       │                                                                     │
│       ▼                                                                     │
│  STEP 2: IDENTIFY BOTTLENECK                                               │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Question 1: Is it network latency?                                 │   │
│  │  - Check if user is far from region (CloudFront needed)             │   │
│  │  - Check DNS resolution time                                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Question 2: Is it database?                                        │   │
│  │  - Check RDS CPU, connections, slow query logs                      │   │
│  │  - Missing indexes?                                                 │   │
│  │  - Lock contention?                                                 │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Question 3: Is it application code?                                │   │
│  │  - Check CPU/memory on EC2/Lambda                                   │   │
│  │  - Check GC logs (Java)                                             │   │
│  │  - N+1 queries?                                                     │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Question 4: Is it external API?                                    │   │
│  │  - Check timeouts, retries                                          │   │
│  │  - Circuit breaker open?                                            │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│       │                                                                     │
│       ▼                                                                     │
│  STEP 3: APPLY FIXES (order by impact/ease)                                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  QUICK WINS (5-10 minutes):                                         │   │
│  │  □ Add database indexes                                             │   │
│  │  □ Enable query caching (Redis)                                     │   │
│  │  □ Increase connection pool size                                    │   │
│  │  □ Add pagination (limit 100)                                       │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  MEDIUM FIXES (1-2 hours):                                          │   │
│  │  □ Add CDN (CloudFront) for static assets                          │   │
│  │  □ Implement response compression (gzip)                            │   │
│  │  □ Reduce payload size (return only needed fields)                  │   │
│  │  □ Parallelize independent calls (CompletableFuture)                │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  LONG-TERM FIXES (1-2 days):                                        │   │
│  │  □ Add read replicas (if read-heavy)                               │   │
│  │  □ Implement caching strategy (Redis)                               │   │
│  │  □ Refactor slow queries (avoid N+1)                                │   │
│  │  □ Add auto scaling (if CPU-bound)                                  │   │
│  │  □ Move to async processing (SQS for heavy tasks)                   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Real-World Optimization Examples

```
CASE STUDY 1: Database Query Optimization
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  Problem: GET /api/orders?user_id=123 takes 5 seconds                      │
│                                                                             │
│  Investigation:                                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  - RDS slow query log shows: SELECT * FROM orders WHERE user_id=123│   │
│  │  - Explain plan: Seq Scan (full table scan) on 10M rows             │   │
│  │  - Missing index on user_id column                                  │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Fix:                                                                       │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  CREATE INDEX idx_orders_user_id ON orders(user_id);                │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Result: 5 seconds → 10 milliseconds (500x improvement)             │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

CASE STUDY 2: N+1 Query Problem
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  Problem: GET /api/users with their orders takes 3 seconds                 │
│                                                                             │
│  Bad Code (N+1 queries):                                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  List<User> users = userRepository.findAll();  // 1 query           │   │
│  │  for (User user : users) {                                          │   │
│  │      List<Order> orders = orderRepository.findByUserId(user.getId());│   │
│  │      // N queries (N = number of users)                             │   │
│  │  }                                                                  │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Fix (Single query with JOIN):                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  @Query("SELECT u, o FROM User u LEFT JOIN FETCH u.orders o")       │   │
│  │  List<User> findAllWithOrders();  // 1 query                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Result: 3 seconds → 200 milliseconds (15x improvement)             │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

CASE STUDY 3: Caching Implementation
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  Problem: GET /api/products/{id} takes 100ms (database each time)          │
│                                                                             │
│  Solution: Redis Cache                                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  public Product getProduct(Long id) {                               │   │
│  │      // Check cache first                                           │   │
│  │      Product cached = redis.get("product:" + id);                   │   │
│  │      if (cached != null) return cached;  // 5ms                    │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │      // Cache miss - query database                                 │   │
│  │      Product product = productRepository.findById(id);  // 100ms    │   │
│  │      redis.set("product:" + id, product, Duration.ofMinutes(60));   │   │
│  │      return product;                                                │   │
│  │  }                                                                  │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Result: 100ms → 5ms (20x improvement, 95% cache hit rate)          │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Optimization Checklist

```
API PERFORMANCE OPTIMIZATION - COMPLETE CHECKLIST:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  ☐ DATABASE OPTIMIZATIONS                                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  □ Add missing indexes (check slow query log)                       │   │
│  │  □ Avoid SELECT * (only fetch needed columns)                       │   │
│  │  □ Use connection pooling (HikariCP - default 10, increase to 50)   │   │
│  │  □ Implement pagination (LIMIT/OFFSET or cursor-based)              │   │
│  │  □ Add read replicas for read-heavy endpoints                       │   │
│  │  □ Use batch operations for multiple inserts/updates                │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ☐ CACHING STRATEGIES                                                       │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  □ Add Redis cache for frequently accessed data                     │   │
│  │  □ Implement CDN (CloudFront) for static assets                     │   │
│  │  □ Add HTTP caching headers (Cache-Control, ETag)                   │   │
│  │  □ Cache database query results (Spring Cache)                      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ☐ APPLICATION OPTIMIZATIONS                                                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  □ Use async processing for non-critical tasks (SQS)                │   │
│  │  □ Parallelize independent calls (CompletableFuture)                │   │
│  │  □ Reduce payload size (return only needed fields)                  │   │
│  │  □ Enable gzip compression                                          │   │
│  │  □ Use DTOs instead of entities                                     │   │
│  │  □ Avoid N+1 queries (use JOIN FETCH)                               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ☐ INFRASTRUCTURE OPTIMIZATIONS                                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  □ Add auto scaling based on CPU/memory                             │   │
│  │  □ Use larger instance types (if CPU/memory bound)                  │   │
│  │  □ Deploy to multiple AZs (reduce latency)                          │   │
│  │  □ Use CloudFront for global users                                  │   │
│  │  □ Enable ALB slow start for new instances                          │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## ❓ Q25. System crashes during peak load, what will you do?

### 1. Immediate Response (First 5 minutes)

```
CRASH DURING PEAK LOAD - INCIDENT RESPONSE:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  IMMEDIATE ACTIONS (0-5 minutes) - STOP THE BLEEDING!                      │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  1. ROLLBACK (if recent deployment)                                 │   │
│  │     ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐      │   │
│  │     │  aws deploy rollback --deployment-id xxx                │      │   │
│  │     │  OR switch traffic back to blue environment             │      │   │
│  │     └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘      │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  2. SCALE UP (if CPU/memory issue)                                  │   │
│  │     ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐      │   │
│  │     │  - Increase instance size (t3.large → r5.4xlarge)      │      │   │
│  │     │  - Increase Auto Scaling max capacity                  │      │   │
│  │     │  - Add more read replicas                              │      │   │
│  │     └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘      │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  3. THROTTLE REQUESTS (protect what's left)                         │   │
│  │     ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐      │   │
│  │     │  - API Gateway: Enable rate limiting (1000/sec)        │      │   │
│  │     │  - WAF: Add rate-based rule                            │      │   │
│  │     │  - ALB: Connection draining, slow start                │      │   │
│  │     └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘      │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  4. QUEUE (buffer incoming requests)                                │   │
│  │     ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐      │   │
│  │     │  - Send requests to SQS instead of direct processing   │      │   │
│  │     │  - Process asynchronously                               │      │   │
│  │     │  - Return 202 Accepted immediately                      │      │   │
│  │     └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Root Cause Analysis (5-30 minutes)

```
ROOT CAUSE ANALYSIS - SYSTEMATIC APPROACH:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  CHECK THESE IN ORDER:                                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  □ Recent Deployment?                                               │   │
│  │    - Check CodeDeploy history                                       │   │
│  │    - Rollback if deployment within last hour                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  □ Database Issues?                                                 │   │
│  │    - Check RDS CPU (100%?)                                          │   │
│  │    - Check connections (maxed out?)                                 │   │
│  │    - Check slow query log                                           │   │
│  │    - Check locks (SELECT * FROM pg_locks)                           │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  □ Resource Exhaustion?                                             │   │
│  │    - EC2 CPU > 90%?                                                 │   │
│  │    - Memory leak?                                                   │   │
│  │    - Disk full? (/var/log)                                          │   │
│  │    - File descriptor limit?                                         │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  □ External Dependency?                                             │   │
│  │    - Payment gateway down?                                          │   │
│  │    - Third-party API timeout?                                       │   │
│  │    - DNS resolution failing?                                        │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  □ Configuration Issue?                                             │   │
│  │    - Connection pool too small?                                     │   │
│  │    - Thread pool exhausted?                                         │   │
│  │    - Timeout values too high?                                       │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  □ Security Issue?                                                  │   │
│  │    - DDoS attack? (check CloudWatch)                               │   │
│  │    - Brute force login attempts?                                    │   │
│  │    - WAF blocking legitimate traffic?                               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Long-term Fixes

```
LONG-TERM PREVENTION STRATEGIES:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  ☐ AUTO SCALING (Prevent future crashes)                                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  □ Configure proper scaling policies:                               │   │
│  │    - CPU > 70% for 2 min → scale out                               │   │
│  │    - Memory > 80% for 2 min → scale out                            │   │
│  │    - SQS queue depth > 1000 → scale out                            │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  □ Pre-warming: Scale up BEFORE peak hours                         │   │
│  │    - Scheduled scaling for 9 AM and 6 PM                           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ☐ CIRCUIT BREAKERS (Handle failures gracefully)                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  @Service                                                           │   │
│  │  public class PaymentService {                                      │   │
│  │      @CircuitBreaker(name = "paymentService", fallbackMethod = "fallback")│
│  │      public Payment processPayment(Order order) {                   │   │
│  │          // Call external payment API                               │   │
│  │      }                                                              │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │      public Payment fallback(Order order, Exception e) {            │   │
│  │          // Return cached response or queue for later              │   │
│  │      }                                                              │   │
│  │  }                                                                  │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ☐ LOAD TESTING (Simulate peak traffic)                                    │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  □ Use JMeter / Locust to simulate 10x normal traffic              │   │
│  │  □ Test auto scaling response time                                  │   │
│  │  □ Identify breaking points                                         │   │
│  │  □ Run weekly during off-peak hours                                 │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ☐ CHAOS ENGINEERING (Test failure scenarios)                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  □ AWS Fault Injection Simulator:                                   │   │
│  │    - Kill random EC2 instances                                      │   │
│  │    - Increase latency on RDS                                        │   │
│  │    - Throttle external APIs                                         │   │
│  │  □ Verify system recovers automatically                             │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```
