## ❓ Q26. How do you handle millions of requests?

### 1. Complete High-Throughput Architecture

```
MILLIONS OF REQUESTS - PRODUCTION ARCHITECTURE:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  LAYER 1: GLOBAL EDGE (Handle 90% of traffic)                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  User (India) ──→ CloudFront (CDN) ──→ Cache hit (90% requests)     │   │
│  │                      │                 Return in 5ms                 │   │
│  │                      │                                               │   │
│  │                      └── Cache miss (10% requests) ──→ Origin       │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  LAYER 2: ENTRY & THROTTLING (Protect backend)                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐            │   │
│  │  │   WAF    │→│  Shield  │→│ API GW   │→│   ALB    │            │   │
│  │  │ (Filter) │  │ (DDoS)   │  │(Rate limit)│  │ (LB)     │            │   │
│  │  └──────────┘  └──────────┘  └──────────┘  └──────────┘            │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Rate Limiting: 10,000 requests per second per API key              │   │
│  │  Burst: 20,000 requests                                             │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  LAYER 3: STATELESS COMPUTE (Scale horizontally)                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │              Auto Scaling Group (200-1000 instances)         │   │   │
│  │  │  ┌─────┐ ┌─────┐ ┌─────┐ ┌─────┐ ┌─────┐ ┌─────┐           │   │   │
│  │  │  │EC2-1│ │EC2-2│ │EC2-3│ │EC2-4│ │EC2-5│ │EC2-6│ ... 1000   │   │   │
│  │  │  └─────┘ └─────┘ └─────┘ └─────┘ └─────┘ └─────┘           │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  OR Serverless: Lambda (10,000+ concurrent executions)              │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  LAYER 4: CACHING (Reduce database load)                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │         ElastiCache Redis Cluster (Sharded)                  │   │   │
│  │  │  ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐           │   │   │
│  │  │  │Shard 1  │ │Shard 2  │ │Shard 3  │ │Shard 4  │           │   │   │
│  │  │  │Primary  │ │Primary  │ │Primary  │ │Primary  │           │   │   │
│  │  │  │+Replica │ │+Replica │ │+Replica │ │+Replica │           │   │   │
│  │  │  └─────────┘ └─────────┘ └─────────┘ └─────────┘           │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Cache Hit Ratio: 95%+                                              │   │
│  │  Cache Latency: <1ms                                                │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  LAYER 5: DATABASE (Scalable storage)                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │  Option 1: DynamoDB (auto-sharding, unlimited scale)         │   │   │
│  │  │  - 10M+ writes/sec                                           │   │   │
│  │  │  - Single-digit ms latency                                    │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │  Option 2: RDS with sharding (for complex queries)           │   │   │
│  │  │  - Shard by user_id across 100+ instances                    │   │   │
│  │  │  - Each shard: 1 primary + 5 read replicas                   │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  LAYER 6: ASYNC PROCESSING (Background tasks)                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────┐    ┌─────────┐    ┌─────────┐    ┌─────────┐          │   │
│  │  │   SQS   │───→│   SQS   │───→│ Lambda  │───→│   S3    │          │   │
│  │  │ (Queue) │    │ (DLQ)   │    │ Worker  │    │(Output) │          │   │
│  │  └─────────┘    └─────────┘    └─────────┘    └─────────┘          │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  - Email sending, report generation, data processing                │   │
│  │  - Not time-critical (can be delayed)                               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Request Flow for 1 Million Requests/Second

```
REQUEST FLOW - 1M REQUESTS PER SECOND:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  Step 1: CDN (CloudFront)                                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  1,000,000 req/sec ──→ 900,000 cache hits (return in 5ms)          │   │
│  │                    └──→ 100,000 go to origin                        │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  Step 2: API Gateway + WAF                                                 │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  100,000 req/sec ──→ Rate limiting (1,000 per IP)                   │   │
│  │                    └──→ 95,000 pass through                         │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  Step 3: ALB + Auto Scaling Group                                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  95,000 req/sec distributed across 500 EC2 instances                │   │
│  │  = 190 req/sec per instance (easily handled by t3.large)           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  Step 4: Redis Cache (95% hit rate)                                       │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  95,000 requests ──→ 90,250 cache hits (1ms)                        │   │
│  │                  └──→ 4,750 cache misses → DynamoDB (5ms)           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  Step 5: DynamoDB (auto-sharding)                                         │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  4,750 writes/sec (well within DynamoDB limits)                     │   │
│  │  Auto-sharding distributes across 100+ partitions                   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  TOTAL LATENCY: ~10-15ms (p99)                                            │
│  TOTAL COST: ~$5,000-10,000/day (depending on configuration)              │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"For millions of requests, I use a layered approach. First, CloudFront CDN caches 90%+ of static traffic. API Gateway with rate limiting protects the backend. The compute layer uses Auto Scaling Groups - we pre-warm before expected peaks. Redis cache reduces database load by 95%+. For the database, DynamoDB auto-shards and handles unlimited scale. Async tasks go to SQS. This architecture handles 1M+ requests per second with sub-10ms latency for cached requests and 50ms for dynamic requests."*

**Key metrics to mention:**

- **Cache hit ratio** - Target 95%+
- **Auto scaling** - Pre-warmed, predictive scaling
- **Database** - DynamoDB for key-value, sharded RDS for complex queries
- **Async** - SQS for non-critical tasks
- **CDN** - CloudFront for global distribution

---

## ❓ Q27. Design URL Shortener using AWS

### 1. Requirements

```
URL SHORTENER - REQUIREMENTS:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  Functional Requirements:                                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  - Shorten URL: POST /shorten → returns short code (abc123)         │   │
│  │  - Redirect: GET /{code} → 301 redirect to original URL             │   │
│  │  - Optional: Custom short codes, analytics, expiration              │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Non-Functional Requirements:                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  - High availability (99.99%)                                       │   │
│  │  - Low latency (redirect < 50ms)                                    │   │
│  │  - Scalable (millions of URLs)                                      │   │
│  │  - Durable (no data loss)                                           │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Complete Architecture

```
URL SHORTENER - AWS ARCHITECTURE:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  CREATE SHORT URL FLOW:                                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  POST /shorten {"url": "https://very-long-url.com/..."}             │   │
│  │       │                                                              │   │
│  │       ▼                                                              │   │
│  │  API Gateway + Lambda Authorizer (rate limit: 1000 per hour)        │   │
│  │       │                                                              │   │
│  │       ▼                                                              │   │
│  │  Lambda Function (CreateShortUrl):                                  │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  1. Validate URL                                            │    │   │
│  │  │  2. Generate short code (Base62 encoding of ID)             │    │   │
│  │  │     - Check DynamoDB for uniqueness                         │    │   │
│  │  │     - Retry if collision (extremely rare)                   │    │   │
│  │  │  3. Store in DynamoDB:                                      │    │   │
│  │  │     PK: short_code, SK: metadata, TTL: expiry               │    │   │
│  │  │  4. Return: {"short_url": "https://short.link/abc123"}      │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  REDIRECT FLOW:                                                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  GET /abc123                                                        │   │
│  │       │                                                              │   │
│  │       ▼                                                              │   │
│  │  CloudFront (CDN) + API Gateway                                     │   │
│  │       │                                                              │   │
│  │       ▼                                                              │   │
│  │  Lambda Function (Redirect):                                        │   │
│  │  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │   │
│  │  │  1. Query DynamoDB by short_code                            │    │   │
│  │  │  2. If found:                                                │    │   │
│  │  │     - Log analytics (SQS async)                             │    │   │
│  │  │     - Return 301 redirect                                    │    │   │
│  │  │  3. If not found: Return 404                                 │    │   │
│  │  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │   │
│  │       │                                                              │   │
│  │       ▼                                                              │   │
│  │  301 Redirect to original URL                                      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  ANALYTICS (Async):                                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Redirect Lambda ──→ SQS Queue ──→ Analytics Lambda                 │   │
│  │                              │                                       │   │
│  │                              ▼                                       │   │
│  │                         DynamoDB (analytics table)                   │   │
│  │                         - Click count, referrer, geo, timestamp     │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  Or use Kinesis for real-time analytics                              │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. DynamoDB Schema

```json
// DynamoDB Table: short_urls
{
  "TableName": "short_urls",
  "KeySchema": [
    {"AttributeName": "short_code", "KeyType": "HASH"}  // Partition key
  ],
  "AttributeDefinitions": [
    {"AttributeName": "short_code", "AttributeType": "S"},
    {"AttributeName": "user_id", "AttributeType": "S"}  // For GSI
  ],
  "GlobalSecondaryIndexes": [
    {
      "IndexName": "user_urls_index",
      "KeySchema": [
        {"AttributeName": "user_id", "KeyType": "HASH"},
        {"AttributeName": "created_at", "KeyType": "RANGE"}
      ]
    }
  ],
  "BillingMode": "PAY_PER_REQUEST",  // Auto-scaling
  "TTL": {"AttributeName": "expiry", "Enabled": true}
}

// Sample item:
{
  "short_code": "abc123",
  "long_url": "https://very-long-url.com/...",
  "user_id": "user123",
  "created_at": "2024-01-15T10:00:00Z",
  "expiry": 1705312800,  // Unix timestamp (TTL)
  "clicks": 0,
  "custom_slug": "my-custom-name"  // Optional
}
```

### 4. Lambda Code (Java)

```java
public class UrlShortenerHandler implements RequestHandler<APIGatewayProxyRequestEvent, APIGatewayProxyResponseEvent> {
    
    private final DynamoDbClient dynamoDb;
    private final SqsClient sqs;
    
    // POST /shorten
    public APIGatewayProxyResponseEvent createShortUrl(APIGatewayProxyRequestEvent request) {
        CreateUrlRequest createRequest = parseRequest(request.getBody());
        
        // Generate short code
        String shortCode = generateShortCode();
        
        // Store in DynamoDB
        PutItemRequest putRequest = PutItemRequest.builder()
            .tableName("short_urls")
            .item(Map.of(
                "short_code", AttributeValue.builder().s(shortCode).build(),
                "long_url", AttributeValue.builder().s(createRequest.getUrl()).build(),
                "user_id", AttributeValue.builder().s(getUserId(request)).build(),
                "created_at", AttributeValue.builder().s(Instant.now().toString()).build()
            ))
            .build();
        
        dynamoDb.putItem(putRequest);
        
        return APIGatewayProxyResponseEvent.builder()
            .withStatusCode(200)
            .withBody("{\"short_url\": \"https://short.link/" + shortCode + "\"}")
            .build();
    }
    
    // GET /{short_code}
    public APIGatewayProxyResponseEvent redirect(String shortCode) {
        // Query DynamoDB
        GetItemRequest getRequest = GetItemRequest.builder()
            .tableName("short_urls")
            .key(Map.of("short_code", AttributeValue.builder().s(shortCode).build()))
            .build();
        
        GetItemResponse response = dynamoDb.getItem(getRequest);
        
        if (!response.hasItem()) {
            return APIGatewayProxyResponseEvent.builder()
                .withStatusCode(404)
                .withBody("{\"error\": \"URL not found\"}")
                .build();
        }
        
        String longUrl = response.item().get("long_url").s();
        
        // Send analytics to SQS (async)
        sendAnalyticsEvent(shortCode);
        
        // Return 301 redirect
        return APIGatewayProxyResponseEvent.builder()
            .withStatusCode(301)
            .withHeaders(Map.of("Location", longUrl))
            .build();
    }
    
    private String generateShortCode() {
        // Base62 encoding (a-zA-Z0-9) of auto-increment ID
        // Using Snowflake ID or Redis INCR for distributed ID generation
        long id = redis.incr("global_counter");
        return Base62.encode(id);
    }
}
```

### 5. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"For URL shortener, I'd use API Gateway + Lambda + DynamoDB. It's serverless, scales automatically, and has low latency. The shorten endpoint generates a unique code (Base62 encoding of a distributed ID) and stores it in DynamoDB. The redirect endpoint queries DynamoDB and returns a 301 redirect. For analytics, we send events to SQS for async processing. DynamoDB's TTL feature automatically expires old URLs. This architecture handles millions of URLs and billions of redirects with sub-50ms latency."*

## ❓ Q28. Design Notification System

### 1. Requirements

```
NOTIFICATION SYSTEM - REQUIREMENTS:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  Functional Requirements:                                                  │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  - Send notifications via Email, SMS, Push, Slack                   │   │
│  │  - Users can set preferences (email only, SMS only, both)           │   │
│  │  - Rate limiting per user (100 emails/hour)                         │   │
│  │  - Retry on failure (exponential backoff)                           │   │
│  │  - Track delivery status                                            │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
│  Non-Functional Requirements:                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  - High throughput (10M notifications/day)                          │   │
│  │  - Reliable (no lost notifications)                                 │   │
│  │  - Low latency (send within 1 second)                               │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2. Complete Architecture

```
NOTIFICATION SYSTEM - AWS ARCHITECTURE:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                             │
│  EVENT SOURCE (Any service)                                                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Order Service, User Service, etc. ──→ Publish to EventBridge       │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    EventBridge (Event Bus)                          │   │
│  │  Rules:                                                            │   │
│  │  - event.type = "order.created" → Send to Notification Service     │   │
│  │  - event.type = "payment.received" → Send to Notification Service  │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │              Notification Service (Lambda + SQS)                    │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    PROCESS PER USER (Fan-out)                       │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  For each user, check preferences:                                  │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │  User Preferences:                                            │   │   │
│  │  │  - email: user@example.com                                   │   │   │
│  │  │  - sms: +1234567890                                          │   │   │
│  │  │  - push: push_token                                          │   │   │
│  │  │  - channels: ["email", "sms"]                                │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │  Send to appropriate SQS queues:                             │   │   │
│  │  │                                                               │   │   │
│  │  │  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐    │   │   │
│  │  │  │Email Queue│  │ SMS Queue │  │Push Queue│  │Slack Queue│    │   │   │
│  │  │  └────┬─────┘  └────┬─────┘  └────┬─────┘  └────┬─────┘    │   │   │
│  │  │       │             │             │             │           │   │   │
│  │  │       ▼             ▼             ▼             ▼           │   │   │
│  │  │  SES Lambda    SNS Lambda    SNS Lambda    Slack Lambda     │   │   │
│  │  │  (Email)       (SMS)         (Push)        (Webhook)        │   │   │
│  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                    │                                        │
│                                    ▼                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    DELIVERY & RETRY                                 │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  On failure:                                                         │   │
│  │  - Retry 3 times with exponential backoff (1s, 2s, 4s)             │   │
│  │  - After 3 failures → Send to Dead Letter Queue (DLQ)               │   │
│  │  - DLQ triggers alert for manual review                             │   │
│  │                                                                      │   │
│  │  On success:                                                        │   │
│  │  - Update DynamoDB (notification status)                            │   │
│  │  - Send to analytics (Kinesis → Redshift)                          │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. Implementation Details

```java
// Notification Service Lambda
public class NotificationService {
    
    public void handleEvent(NotificationEvent event) {
        String userId = event.getUserId();
        String message = event.getMessage();
        
        // Get user preferences from DynamoDB
        UserPreferences prefs = getPreferences(userId);
        
        // Fan-out to channels
        for (Channel channel : prefs.getChannels()) {
            sendToChannel(channel, userId, message);
        }
    }
    
    private void sendToChannel(Channel channel, String userId, String message) {
        String queueUrl = getQueueUrl(channel);
        
        SendMessageRequest request = SendMessageRequest.builder()
            .queueUrl(queueUrl)
            .messageBody(message)
            .messageAttributes(Map.of(
                "userId", MessageAttributeValue.builder()
                    .dataType("String")
                    .stringValue(userId)
                    .build()
            ))
            .delaySeconds(getDelaySeconds(channel))  // SMS has higher delay
            .build();
        
        sqsClient.sendMessage(request);
    }
}

// Email Sender (SQS Consumer)
@Component
public class EmailSender {
    
    @SqsListener("email-queue")
    public void sendEmail(EmailRequest request) {
        try {
            SendEmailRequest email = SendEmailRequest.builder()
                .destination(Destination.builder()
                    .toAddresses(request.getUserEmail())
                    .build())
                .message(Message.builder()
                    .subject(Content.builder()
                        .data(request.getSubject())
                        .build())
                    .body(Body.builder()
                        .text(Content.builder()
                            .data(request.getMessage())
                            .build())
                        .build())
                    .build())
                .build();
            
            sesClient.sendEmail(email);
            
        } catch (Exception e) {
            // Throw exception to trigger SQS retry
            throw new RetryableException("Failed to send email", e);
        }
    }
}

// Rate Limiting (per user)
@Component
public class RateLimiter {
    
    private final RedisTemplate<String, Integer> redis;
    
    public boolean allowRequest(String userId, String channel, int limit) {
        String key = "ratelimit:" + channel + ":" + userId;
        String window = "3600";  // 1 hour
        
        Long current = redis.opsForValue().increment(key);
        if (current == 1) {
            redis.expire(key, Long.parseLong(window), TimeUnit.SECONDS);
        }
        
        return current <= limit;
    }
}
```

### 4. Interview Tips

**What interviewers expect:**

✅ *"For a notification system, I use EventBridge to receive events from various services. A Lambda function checks user preferences and fans out to different SQS queues - one for email, one for SMS, one for push. Each queue has a dedicated Lambda consumer that calls the respective AWS service (SES for email, SNS for SMS, SNS for push). We implement rate limiting per user using Redis. Failed messages go to a DLQ after 3 retries. This architecture is fully serverless, scales automatically, and guarantees at-least-once delivery."*

---

# 💡 PRO TIPS (Very Important)

## What Interviewers Actually Want:

```
INTERVIEWER EXPECTATIONS - DON'T JUST DEFINE, DEMONSTRATE:

❌ Bad Answer: "SQS is a message queue."

✅ Good Answer: "SQS decouples our order service from payment processing. 
When an order comes in, we put it in SQS and return immediately. 
The payment service processes at its own pace. 
During Black Friday, SQS buffers 10M messages without breaking a sweat. 
We use a DLQ for failed payments and have alerts when queue depth exceeds 50K."

❌ Bad Answer: "DynamoDB is a NoSQL database."

✅ Good Answer: "DynamoDB is perfect for our shopping cart. 
Access pattern is simple - get by user_id. 
We need single-digit ms latency and auto-scaling during flash sales. 
We use DynamoDB's TTL to expire abandoned carts after 7 days. 
For reporting, we stream changes to S3 via DynamoDB Streams and query with Athena."

Key patterns to demonstrate:
1. Problem → Solution → Why this service → Alternatives considered
2. Real numbers (latency, throughput, cost)
3. Trade-offs (pros/cons of your choice)
4. Failure scenarios (what if X fails?)
5. Scaling strategy (how to handle 10x growth)
```

## Answer Framework (Always Use):

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    GOLDEN ANSWER FRAMEWORK                                  │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  1. STATE THE PROBLEM                                                       │
│     "We needed to handle 10,000 orders per second..."                       │
│                                                                             │
│  2. EXPLAIN YOUR SOLUTION                                                   │
│     "...so we used SQS between order and payment services."                 │
│                                                                             │
│  3. JUSTIFY WHY (Trade-offs)                                               │
│     "SQS gives us unlimited throughput and 14-day persistence.              │
│      We considered RabbitMQ but didn't want to manage servers."             │
│                                                                             │
│  4. ADD REAL NUMBERS                                                        │
│     "In production, we process 50K messages/second with                    │
│      p99 latency of 5ms. Cost is $200/month."                               │
│                                                                             │
│  5. DISCUSS FAILURE SCENARIOS                                               │
│     "If payment service fails, messages stay in SQS for 14 days.           │
│      We have a DLQ after 3 retries."                                        │
│                                                                             │
│  6. MENTION SCALING                                                         │
│     "SQS scales automatically. We just add more consumers."                │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## Final Revision Notes (Last 10 minutes before interview):

```
QUICK REVISION - AWS SERVICES CHEAT SHEET:

Compute:
- EC2: Virtual machines (IaaS)
- Lambda: Serverless functions (FaaS)
- ECS: Containers (Docker)
- Beanstalk: PaaS (just deploy code)

Storage:
- S3: Objects (files, static hosting)
- EBS: Block storage (for EC2)
- EFS: Shared file system
- Glacier: Archive (cheap, slow)

Database:
- RDS: SQL (PostgreSQL, MySQL)
- DynamoDB: NoSQL (key-value)
- ElastiCache: Redis/Memcached (caching)
- Redshift: Data warehouse

Networking:
- VPC: Private network
- ALB/ELB: Load balancer
- CloudFront: CDN
- Route 53: DNS

Messaging:
- SQS: Queue (decoupling)
- SNS: Pub-sub (broadcast)
- EventBridge: Event bus (routing)
- Kinesis: Streaming (real-time)

Security:
- IAM: Users, roles, policies
- Secrets Manager: Secrets storage
- KMS: Encryption keys
- WAF: Web firewall
- Shield: DDoS protection

Monitoring:
- CloudWatch: Metrics + Logs + Alarms
- X-Ray: Tracing
- CloudTrail: API audit

Deployment:
- CodePipeline: CI/CD
- CodeBuild: Build
- CodeDeploy: Deploy
- CloudFormation: Infrastructure as Code

ALWAYS REMEMBER:
1. Stateless > Stateful
2. Cache first, scale later
3. Design for failure
4. Monitor everything
5. Automate everything
```
